The Obligation of Hajj: Conditions and Proofs
Opening of the Book of Hajj with ruling on obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Hajj (fard), list its conditions for obligation, and explain the proof that it is required only once in a lifetime.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard once in a lifetime on every free, Muslim, adult, sane, and able person.

This passage opens the Book of Hajj in the commentary. The author clearly states that Hajj is a fard obligation—so fundamental that denying it constitutes disbelief. He then enumerates the precise conditions that must be met for Hajj to be obligatory, and provides a key hadith establishing that it is required only once. Let's unpack the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Read the opening statement. The author says Hajj is 'fard' and that its denier becomes a disbeliever. Note that the base text uses 'wajib' but the commentary clarifies that in this context it means fard.
Hanafis distinguish fard (certain, denial = kufr) from wajib (probable, denial = not kufr).
2
List the conditions for obligation
The text states: 'upon every free, Muslim, mukallaf.' Then it expands: not obligatory on a slave, disbeliever, insane person, child, blind person, sick person, or one without provisions and mount. Extract each explicit condition and its opposite (preventer).
The commentary lists four types of slaves: mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, qinn.
3
Examine the dalil (hadith)
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Prophet responds to al-Aqra' bin Habis's question about annual Hajj: 'If I said yes, it would be obligatory, and you would not be able to do it; so whoever does more is voluntary.' Identify how this proves the obligation is once.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the ruling is fard due to consensus.
4
Understand the definition of Hajj
The commentary gives linguistic and legal definitions: linguistically 'intention', legally 'visiting the specific place at a specific time.' This foundational definition frames all subsequent rules.
The specific place is the Ka'bah and sacred sites; the specific time is the months of Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج)
اعلم أن الحج فريضةٌ يَكْفُرُ جاحدُهُ لكن أطلق عليه لفظ الوجوب، وأراد الفريضة حيث ، قال : (يجب على كلِّ حُر مسلم مكلف

(۱) فعن ابن عباس ، قال : «يا أيها الناس كتب عليكم الحج قال : فقام الأقرع بن حابس فقال : في كل عام يا رسول الله قال : لو قلتها لوجبت، ولو وجبت لم تعملوا بها أو لم تستطيعوا أن تعملوا بها، فمن زاد فهو تطوع في مسند أحمد» (١: ٢٥٥، ٢٩٠)، و«المستدرك» (١: ٦٤٣»، وصححه الحاكم، وسنن أبي داود (۲) : (۱۳۹) الدارمي (۲) : : ٤٦)، و (سنن البيهقي الكبير (٥) : (۱۷۸) ، و (سنن الدارقطني (۲ : ۲۷۸)
وغيرها.
(۲) في (صحيح ابن خزيمة ) : (٣٤٩) ، و((المستدرك» (۱) : (٦٥٥)، وصححه، وغيرهما.
وسنن
Book of Hajj. Know that Hajj is a fard obligation; its denier becomes a disbeliever. But he used the term 'wajib' and intended fard when he said: 'It is obligatory upon every free, Muslim, mukallaf.' [1] His statement: 'Book of Hajj' – when he finished mentioning the three pillars, he began the fourth pillar. It is, with fath al-ha and tashdid al-jim and kasr al-ha, linguistically: intention, and legally: visiting a specific place at a specific time. (2) His statement: 'obligatory' – i.e., once in a lifetime; anything more is voluntary, as he said. Allah (1) the Prophet – reported by Abu Dawud. [3] His statement: 'upon every free...' etc. So it is not obligatory upon a slave, whether he is a mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, or qinn. This is indicated by the hadith: 'Any slave who performs Hajj, even ten Hajjs, then is freed, must perform the Hajj of Islam' – reported by al-Hakim and authenticated according to the condition of the two Shaykhs. And it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. If a disbeliever possesses the means of ability, then becomes Muslim after becoming poor, it is not obligatory upon him. This is because disbelievers are not addressed regarding the performance of acts of worship, and they are not valid due to the missing condition, which is faith. And it is not obligatory upon one not mukallaf, such as the insane and the child, because the address of obligation is lifted from them. And it is not obligatory upon the blind, the sick, and one unable to [afford] provisions and mount. (1) From Ibn Abbas: 'O people, Hajj has been prescribed for you.' Then al-Aqra' bin Habis said: 'Every year, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'If I said yes, it would be obligatory, and if it were obligatory, you would not be able to do it.' So whoever does more is voluntary. In Musnad Ahmad, etc. (2) In Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah and al-Mustadrak, authenticated by al-Hakim, and others.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hajj in the commentary. The author first clarifies that Hajj is a fard (obligatory) duty; denying its obligation constitutes disbelief. He notes that the base text uses the term 'wajib' but intends the stronger category of 'fard.' The Arabic lexicographical note explains that 'hajj' linguistically means 'intention' and legally means 'visiting the specific place (the Ka'bah and sacred sites) at a specific time (the months of Hajj).' The ruling: Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime; additional performances are voluntary. This is supported by the hadith from Abu Dawud (also in Ahmad and others) where the Prophet said, 'Had I said yes, it would be obligatory, and you would not be able to perform it; so additional Hajj is voluntary.' The conditions for the obligation are then enumerated: one must be free (so slaves are not obligated – the commentary lists four categories of slaves: mudabbar (contract of manumission after master's death), umm walad (slave mother of child), mukatab (contract of manumission for payment), and qinn (ordinary slave)), Muslim (disbelievers are not obligated because they are not addressed for acts of worship, and their acts are invalid for lack of faith), and mukallaf (legally responsible, so the insane and children are excluded). Furthermore, the blind, the sick, and those without ability (zad and rahila – provisions and mount) are not obligated. The text stresses that ability is a condition. The footnotes provide source verification of key hadith.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): Linguistically: intention; legally: visiting the Ka'bah and related sacred sites at the specific time (months of Hajj).
فريضة (farīḍah): A religious obligation whose denial constitutes disbelief.
مكلف (mukallaf): Legally responsible: a free, adult, sane Muslim capable of performing obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on whom is Hajj obligatory?
A) Every free Muslim, adult, sane, and capable.
B) Every Muslim, including slaves and children.
C) Only wealthy Muslims.
D) Every person, regardless of religion.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard once in a lifetime on every free, Muslim, adult, sane, and able person; proof from hadith confirms it is not annual.

Obligation of Hajj: Conditions and Proof
Explaining the obligation of Hajj and who it is obligatory upon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Hajj being obligatory and identify the Hadith proof that it is required only once in a lifetime.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime on every free, Muslim, sane adult who can afford it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the obligation of Hajj, emphasizing that it is a fard (denial leads to kufr) and listing who is exempt. The author explains that although the text uses 'wajib', it means 'fard' in the Hanafi sense. A hadith from Ibn Abbas confirms that Hajj is required only once, and any additional performance is voluntary. Understanding these conditions ensures one knows when Hajj becomes a personal duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Hajj is a religious obligation. Determine the exact ruling: fard (definitive) or wajib? Note the author's clarification.
The author uses 'yajib' but intends 'fard' because denial leads to kufr.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The passage cites the Hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet (ﷺ) answers a question about annual Hajj. Identify this as the proof.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove that Hajj is once? The Prophet explicitly says 'If I said so, it would be obligatory... so what is extra is voluntary.'
The command 'kutiba' indicates obligation, but the reply limits it to once.
4
List the conditions of obligation
The passage specifies conditions: free, Muslim, mukallaf (sane, adult), and ability (health, sight, provisions, mount).
These are shurut al-wujub, not shurut al-sihhah.
5
Note the exemptions
Those not fulfilling conditions are exempt: slaves, disbelievers, children, insane, blind, sick, and those without means.
Exemption does not mean the act is invalid; it means no obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَجِبُ على كلِّ حُرِّ مسلم مكلف
كتاب الحج
اعلم أن الحج فريضةٌ يَكْفُرُ جاحدُهُ لكن أطلق عليه لفظ الوجوب، وأراد الفريضة حيث قال : (يجب على كلِّ حُر مسلم مكلف
[١] قوله : كتاب الحج ؛ لَمَّا فَرَغَ عن ذكرِ الأركانِ الثَّلاثةِ شرعَ فِي الرُّكنِ الرَّابع - وهو بفتح الحاء، وتشديد الجيم، وبكسر الحاء - لغة : القصد، وشرعاً : زيارة مكان مخصوص في وقت مخصوص. (٢) قوله : يجب؛ أي في العمر مرَّةً واحدة، فما زاد فهو تطوع، كذا قال الله النبي ، أخرجه أبو داود. [٣] قوله : على كل حر ... الخ ؛ فلا يجب على عبد مدبراً كان أو أم ولد، أو مكاتباً، أو قناً يدلُّ عليه حديث: «أيما عبد حجّ ولو عشر حجج ثم أعتق فعليه حجة الإسلام ) ، أخرجه الحاكم وصححه على شرط الشيخين، ولا يجب على كافر، فلو ملك الكافر ما به الاستطاعةُ ثمَّ أسلم بعدما افتقر لا يجب عليه ؛ ذلك لأنَّ الكفَّارَ غير مخاطبين في حق أداء العبادات، ولا تصح منها لفوات شرطه وهو الإيمان، ولا يجب على غير مكلف كالمجنون، والصبي ؛ لأنَّ خطاب التكليف مرتفع عنهما، ولا يجب على أعمى، ومريض، وغير قادر على الزَّادِ والراحلة.
(١) فعن ابن عباس ، قال : «يا أيها الناس كتب عليكم الحج قال : فقام الأقرع بن حابس فقال : في كل عام يا رسول الله قال : لو قلتها لوجبت، ولو وجبت لم تعملوا بها أو لم تستطيعوا أن تعملوا بها، فمن زاد فهو تطوع في مسند أحمد» (١: ٢٥٥، ٢٩٠)، و«المستدرك» (١: ٦٤٣)، وصححه الحاكم، وسنن أبي داود (٢) : (۱۳۹) الدارمي (٢) : : ٤٦)، و (سنن البيهقي الكبير (٥) : (۱۷۸) ، و (سنن الدارقطني (٢ : ۲۷۸) وغيرها.
(٢) في (صحيح ابن خزيمة ) : (٣٤٩) ، و((المستدرك» (١) : (٦٥٥)، وصححه، وغيرهما.
It is obligatory upon every free Muslim who is legally responsible. The Book of Hajj. Know that Hajj is an obligatory act such that its denier becomes a disbeliever, but the author used the word 'wujub' and intended 'fard' where he said: (It is obligatory upon every free Muslim who is legally responsible). [1] His saying: 'The Book of Hajj' – when he finished mentioning the three pillars, he began the fourth pillar – and it is with a fatha on the ha and tashdid of the jim, and with kasr of the ha – linguistically: intention, and legally: visiting a specific place at a specific time. (2) His saying: 'obligatory' – i.e., once in a lifetime; whatever additional is voluntary. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said that, reported by Abu Dawud. [3] His saying: 'upon every free...' etc. – so it is not obligatory upon a slave, whether a mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab, or a qinn. The hadith indicates: 'Any slave who performs Hajj even ten times then is freed, he must perform the Hajj of Islam.' Al-Hakim reported it and authenticated it according to the condition of the two shaykhs. It is not obligatory upon a disbeliever; if a disbeliever possesses the means then becomes Muslim after becoming poor, it is not obligatory upon him. That is because the disbelievers are not addressed regarding the performance of acts of worship, and it is not valid from them due to the absence of its condition, which is faith. It is not obligatory upon a non-mukallaf like an insane person and a child because the address of taklif is lifted from them. It is not obligatory upon a blind person, a sick person, and one who is not capable of provisions and a mount. (1) From Ibn Abbas, said: 'O people, Hajj has been prescribed for you.' Al-Aqra' bin Habis stood and said: 'Every year, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'If I said so, it would be obligatory, and if it were obligatory, you would not be able to do it, so what is extra is voluntary.' In Musnad Ahmad, etc. (2) In Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah, etc.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the obligation of Hajj. It begins by defining Hajj linguistically as 'intention' and legally as 'visiting a specific place (the Kaaba and Arafat) at a specific time (the months of Hajj)'. The author clarifies that Hajj is a faridah (definitive obligation) such that its denier becomes a disbeliever, though the text uses the term 'wajib'—in Hanafi terminology, 'fard' is proven by qat'i evidence, while 'wajib' is a broader category. The ruling is that Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime; any additional performance is voluntary, as confirmed by a hadith from Abu Dawud. The passage then lists the conditions for this obligation: the person must be free (not a slave), Muslim, and mukallaf (sane and have reached puberty). Slaves are exempted based on a hadith that a slave who performs Hajj multiple times must still do so after freedom. Disbelievers are not obligated because they are not addressed for the performance of acts of worship, and even if they convert after losing the means, the obligation does not arise. Non-mukallaf (children and the insane) are exempt because the address of taklif is lifted from them. Finally, it mentions that the blind, the sick, and those unable to afford provisions and transport are also not obligated. The proof for the obligation being once in a lifetime is the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly said it is one Hajj, and any extra is voluntary.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): Linguistically 'intending', legally 'visiting a specific place (the Kaaba and Arafat) at a specific time (months of Hajj)'.
فريضة (faridah): An obligatory act proven by definitive evidence; denial entails kufr.
مكلف (mukallaf): A legally responsible person: free, Muslim, sane, and have reached puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a slave who performs Hajj ten times before being freed?
A) The Hajj counts and he does not need to repeat it after freedom.
B) He must perform the Hajj of Islam after being freed.
C) He is exempt from Hajj altogether because he was a slave.
D) His Hajj is valid but only counts as one of the ten.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard once in a lifetime on every free, Muslim, sane adult who is physically and financially able.

Conditions for Hajj Obligation: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Health
Explaining additional conditions for Hajj obligation with an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Hajj obligation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether health is a condition for obligation or performance, including the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Health is a condition for performance, not obligation — the chronically ill must send a proxy.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands the conditions for Hajj obligation beyond the basics: soundness, sight, provisions, mount, and surplus. It also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: is physical health a condition for the very obligation (shart wujub) or only for performing it oneself (shart ada)? The relied-upon view, favoured in Fath al-Qadir, is that even the chronically ill must send a proxy. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the rules of Hajj obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions listed
The passage lists five conditions for Hajj obligation: being sound (sahih), sighted (basir), having provisions (zad), a mount (rahilah), and surplus (fadl). Recognize that these expand upon the general ability (istita'ah).
The conditions are additional to Islam, freedom, maturity, and sanity.
2
Understand the definition of 'sahih' and its immediate ruling
Sahih means free from illnesses that prevent travel, such as paralysis, chronic disease, or extreme old age. The immediate ruling: such a person is not obligated to perform Hajj themselves or by proxy.
This seems absolute, but the next step shows an internal disagreement.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on health
Abu Hanifa holds that health is a condition for the obligation itself (shart wujub) — so the chronically ill have no duty at all. The two companions (Sahibayn) hold that health is a condition for performance (shart ada) — the obligation exists, but they must send a proxy.
The passage notes a riwaya supporting the Sahibayn, and that Fath al-Qadir preferred their view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The mufta bihi is the view of the two companions: the chronically ill must send a proxy. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is derived from the tarjih of al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.
5
Apply the same analysis to the remaining conditions
For basir: blindness exempts even with a guide. For zad and rahilah: provisions and mount must be suitable to one's status. For fadl: surplus over essential needs and dependents' expenses for the entire journey.
These definitions ensure that Hajj does not cause hardship and align with the Quranic verse on istita'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صحيح بصير
[١] قوله : صحيح ؛ أي سالم عن الأمراض المانعة عن القيام بما لا بد منه في السفر، فلا يجب على مقعد ومفلوج وشيخ كبير لا يستطيع على الراحلة بنفسه، وأعمى وإن وجد قائداً ، أو محبوس وغيرهم، لا بأنفسهم ولا بالنيابة، وفي رواية : وجوب الإحجاج عليهم، وهذا قولهما ، فعندهما الصحة من شرائط وجوب الأداء ، وعنده من شرائط الوجوب، ورجح في «الفتح»(۳) قولهما. (۲) قوله : بصير؛ أورد عليه أنه لا حاجة إلى ذكره بعد ذكر الصحيح ، فإنّ العمى نوع من المرض.
وأجيب عنه : بأنه ذكره اهتماماً ؛ لئلا يتوهم دخول الأعمى في الصحيح ؛ لأنه لا يطلق المريض عليه في العرف غالباً.
[۳] قوله : زاد ؛ هو قدر ما يكتري به جانب محمل ، وينتفع به، ويصح به بدنه ، فالمعتاد لأكل اللحم ، لو قدر على خبز وجبن، ومعتاد المحمل والهودج لو قدر على الإكاف لا يعد قادراً، وهذا هو المراد بقوله تعالى : ( وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيهِ سَبِيلا ) [٤]قوله : فضلاً ؛ أي حال كونه فاضلاً عن حوائجه الأصلية كالمسكن والملبس وأثاث البيت، وفاضلا عن نفقة من عليه نفقته، وهو المراد بالعيال بالكسر، ويعتبر أن يكون القدرة على ذلك. ، من حين ذهابه إلى زمان رجوعه إلى وطنه.
Sound, sighted, having provisions and a mount, surplus. [1] His saying: 'sound' – i.e., free from illnesses that prevent undertaking what is necessary in travel. So it is not obligatory upon a paralyzed person, a cripple, a very old person who cannot mount the riding animal by himself, or a blind person even if he finds a guide, or a prisoner, and others, neither by themselves nor by proxy. And in one narration: it is obligatory to have Hajj performed for them; this is their (the two companions) view. According to them, health is a condition for the obligation of performance, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is a condition for the very obligation. In 'al-Fath' (Fath al-Qadir) he preponderated their view. (2) His saying: 'sighted' – an objection was raised that there is no need to mention it after mentioning sound, since blindness is a type of illness. And it is answered: that he mentioned it out of emphasis, lest one think that the blind is included in 'sound' because he is not usually called 'sick' in common usage. [3] His saying: 'provisions' – it is the amount with which one can hire a side of a litter and benefit from it and with which his body becomes sound. So one accustomed to eating meat, if he can afford bread and cheese, and one accustomed to a litter and howdah, if he can afford a pack-saddle, is not considered capable. This is what is meant by His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House - for whoever is able to find thereto a way.' [4] His saying: 'surplus' – i.e., in the state of being surplus over his original needs like housing, clothing, and household furnishings, and surplus over the maintenance of those whom he must support, and what is meant by dependents (with a kasra). It is considered that he has the ability for that from the time of his departure until the time of his return to his homeland.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage expands on the conditions for Hajj obligation. It begins by explaining 'sahih' (soundness): a person free from illnesses that prevent travel, such as paralysis, chronic disease, or extreme old age. Such a person is not obligated to perform Hajj themselves or by proxy. However, an intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, health is a condition for the very obligation (shart wujub) – so such a person has no duty at all. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), health is a condition for performance (shart ada) – so the duty exists, but they must send a proxy. The author of Fath al-Qadir preferred the view of the two companions, making the mufta bihi that a chronically ill person must send someone to perform Hajj on their behalf. Next, 'basir' (sighted) is discussed. Although it might seem redundant after 'sahih', it is mentioned to emphasize that a blind person is not considered 'sahih' in common usage, and thus the blind are not obligated. Then, 'zad' (provisions) and 'rahilah' (mount) are defined: provisions must be sufficient to sustain the body and hire transport appropriate to one's status. If one is accustomed to luxury but can only afford basic provisions, they are not considered capable. This interprets the Quranic verse on istita'ah (ability). Finally, 'fadlan' (surplus) means having enough beyond essential needs (housing, clothing, furniture) and the expenses of dependents for the entire journey. All these conditions ensure that Hajj does not cause undue hardship.

Key Terms
صحيح (sahih): Free from illnesses that prevent travel, such as paralysis, chronic disease, or extreme old age.
بصير (basir): Sighted; a blind person is not obligated even with a guide.
زاد (zad): Provisions sufficient to sustain the body and hire appropriate transport.
راحلة (rahilah): Mount or means of transport, which may be hired, appropriate to the person's status.
فضل (fadl): Surplus beyond essential needs (housing, clothing, furniture) and dependents' expenses for the journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding a chronically ill person who cannot travel?
A) No obligation at all, even by proxy.
B) They must send someone to perform Hajj on their behalf.
C) They are not obligated because health is a condition for obligation.
D) They must perform Hajj themselves if they can afford a stretcher.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position is that health is a condition for performing Hajj oneself, not for the obligation itself, so a chronically ill person must arrange a proxy.

Conditions for Hajj Obligation in the Hanafi School
Lists and explains conditions for Hajj obligation with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for Hajj obligation in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi differences regarding health and road safety conditions.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when one is physically and financially able, the road is safe, and a woman has a mahram.

The obligation of Hajj is not automatic upon reaching puberty; it is conditional upon specific legal prerequisites derived from the Quranic concept of istita'ah (ability). This lesson unpacks each condition as explained by the Hanafi school, including the nuanced differences between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn) on whether health and road safety are conditions for the obligation itself or for its performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
Read the opening sentence of the passage carefully: the author lists six prerequisites for Hajj to become obligatory: being physically sound, sighted, having provision and a mount, having a surplus beyond essential needs, safety of the road, and for a woman, a husband or mahram. List them in order.
These are derived from the Quranic phrase 'man istata'a ilayhi sabila' (whoever is able to find a way).
2
Analyze the condition of health and the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage explains that 'sahih' excludes those who cannot travel due to illness or disability. It then notes an internal Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa considers health a condition for the obligation itself, while the Sahibayn consider it a condition for performance. Understand the practical consequence: if a healthy person becomes ill after Hajj becomes due, according to Abu Hanifa he is no longer obligated, but according to the Sahibayn he must still perform it later when able.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as per al-Fath.
3
Define financial capacity (provision and surplus)
Examine the definitions: 'zad' (provision) is not absolute but relative to one's custom – e.g., one accustomed to meat is not considered able if only bread and cheese are available. 'Fadlan' (surplus) means having enough to cover essential needs (housing, clothing, furnishings) and the maintenance of dependents from departure to return. This is a moral and legal consideration to prevent hardship.
The Hanafi definition of istita'ah is broader than mere possession of cash; it includes customary standards.
4
Understand the mahram condition and its evidence
The passage requires a woman to travel with her husband or a mahram (a permanently unmarriageable relative). This is supported by the hadith 'Let no woman perform Hajj unless with a mahram' and the Sahihain hadith prohibiting women from traveling without a mahram. Note that this condition applies regardless of physical or financial ability – even if the woman can afford all expenses, she is not obligated if she cannot secure a mahram.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), so its proof is zanni, but the Hanafi school adheres to it as a condition for obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صحيح بصير، له زاد وراحلة، فضلاً عما لا بد منه، وعن نفقة عياله إلى حين عوده، مع أمن الطريق، والزوج أو المحرم للمرأة. [قوله: صحيح؛ أي سالم عن الأمراض المانعة عن القيام بما لا بد منه في السفر، فلا يجب على مقعد ومفلوج وشيخ كبير لا يستطيع على الراحلة بنفسه، وأعمى وإن وجد قائداً، أو محبوس وغيرهم، لا بأنفسهم ولا بالنيابة، وفي رواية: وجوب الإحجاج عليهم، وهذا قولهما، فعندهما الصحة من شرائط وجوب الأداء، وعنده من شرائط الوجوب، ورجح في «الفتح» قولهما. قوله: بصير؛ أورد عليه أنه لا حاجة إلى ذكره بعد ذكر الصحيح، فإنّ العمى نوع من المرض. وأجيب عنه: بأنه ذكره اهتماماً؛ لئلا يتوهم دخول الأعمى في الصحيح؛ لأنه لا يطلق المريض عليه في العرف غالباً. قوله: زاد؛ هو قدر ما يكتري به جانب محمل، وينتفع به، ويصح به بدنه، فالمعتاد لأكل اللحم، لو قدر على خبز وجبن، ومعتاد المحمل والهودج لو قدر على الإكاف لا يعد قادراً، وهذا هو المراد بقوله تعالى: (وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيهِ سَبِيلا). قوله: فضلاً؛ أي حال كونه فاضلاً عن حوائجه الأصلية كالمسكن والملبس وأثاث البيت، وفاضلاً عن نفقة من عليه نفقته، وهو المراد بالعيال بالكسر، ويعتبر أن يكون القدرة على ذلك من حين ذهابه إلى زمان رجوعه إلى وطنه. قوله: مع أمن الطريق؛ أي كون الطريق من وطنه إلى مكة، وهو أن يكون الغالب فيه السلامة مع عدم غلبة الخوف، وهذا من شرائط الوجوب عنده، وعندهما من شرائط وجوب الأداء، ورجحه في «الفتح»، فيجب الإيصاء به إذا مات قبل أمن الطريق. قوله: والزوج؛ عطف على قوله: «أمن الطريق»؛ أي يشترط أن يكون مع المرأة زوجها أو محرم من محارمها، وهو من يحرم عليه نكاحها تأييداً؛ لحديث: «ألا لا يحجن امرأة إلا ومعها محرم»، أخرجه البزار، وفي الصحيحين: «لا تسافر المرأة إلا مع محرم».
Physically sound, sighted, having provision and a mount, surplus beyond what is necessary, and for the maintenance of his dependents until his return, with safety of the road, and for a woman, her husband or a mahram. [His saying: 'sound' means free from illnesses that prevent undertaking what is necessary in travel, so it is not obligatory upon a paralyzed person, a hemiplegic, an old man who cannot mount the animal himself, a blind person even if he finds a guide, or a prisoner and others, neither by themselves nor by proxy; and in one narration: it is obligatory to have them perform Hajj, and this is their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), for in their view health is a condition for performance obligation, while in his view (Abu Hanifa) it is a condition for the obligation itself, and he preferred their view in al-Fath. His saying: 'sighted' – it was objected that there is no need to mention it after mentioning soundness, because blindness is a type of illness. He answered: he mentioned it out of emphasis, lest one might mistakenly include the blind under 'sound', because the term 'sick' is not generally applied to the blind in common usage. His saying: 'provision' means the amount with which he can hire a side of a howdah, benefit from it, and by which his body is sustained; so one accustomed to eating meat, if he can only afford bread and cheese, and one accustomed to a howdah or litter, if he can only afford a pack-saddle, is not considered able. This is the meaning of His statement: 'And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House, for whoever is able to find a way to it.' His saying: 'surplus' means being surplus over his essential needs like housing, clothing, household furnishings, and surplus over the maintenance of those he is obliged to support, and that is meant by 'dependents'; and it is considered that he has the ability for that from the time of his departure until his return to his homeland. His saying: 'with safety of the road' means the road from his homeland to Mecca, which is that the prevailing condition is safety without predominance of fear; and this is a condition for obligation in his view, while in their view it is a condition for performance obligation, and he preferred it in al-Fath; thus, if he dies before safety of the road, he must bequeath for Hajj. His saying: 'and the husband' is conjuncted to 'safety of the road'; i.e., it is required that the woman have her husband or a mahram from her close relatives, i.e., one whom marriage is permanently prohibited to her, due to the hadith: 'Let no woman perform Hajj unless with a mahram' recorded by al-Bazzar, and in the Sahihain: 'A woman should not travel except with a mahram.'
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions that must be met for Hajj to become obligatory. The author lists six conditions: (1) being physically sound (sahih) – free from debilitating illness so one can travel; (2) being sighted (basir) – mentioned separately to emphasize that the blind are not included even if they have a guide; (3) having provision (zad) sufficient for the journey, including hiring a mount; (4) having surplus (fadlan) beyond basic needs like housing, clothing, and maintaining dependents from departure until return; (5) safety of the road (amn al-tariq) – that the route is predominantly safe; and (6) for women, the presence of a husband or a permanent mahram (one whom she cannot marry). The commentary delves into intra-Hanafi disputes: regarding health, Abu Hanifa considers it a condition for the obligation itself, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a condition for performance; the preferred view in al-Fath is that of the Sahibayn. Similarly, road safety is a condition for obligation according to Abu Hanifa, but for performance according to the Sahibayn. For a woman, the requirement of a mahram is based on authentic hadith.

Key Terms
زاد (zād): Provision sufficient for the journey, including the ability to hire a mount and sustain the body.
راحلة (rāḥilah): A riding animal or any means of transport, even hired, suitable for the person's condition.
فضلاً (faḍlan): Surplus beyond essential needs (housing, clothing, household goods, and dependents' maintenance) from departure to return.
محرم (maḥram): A male relative to whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as father, brother, son, uncle, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Hajj is obligatory but he must send a proxy.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only upon fulfilling six conditions: sound health, sight, provision, financial surplus, safe road, and for women, a husband or mahram.

The Condition of Mahram for a Woman's Hajj
Explains mahram condition with hadith proofs and ikhtilaf on wujub vs ada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of a mahram for a woman's Hajj, cite the primary hadith evidence, and distinguish between the condition for obligation and performance.

Core Idea
A woman must be accompanied by her husband or mahram to perform Hajj, or else she is not obligated.

This lesson examines a fundamental condition for a woman's obligation to perform Hajj: the presence of a husband or mahram. The Hanafi school derives this requirement from explicit hadiths and discusses whether it pertains to the original obligation or its performance. Understanding this condition is crucial for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the condition for a woman's Hajj: she must be accompanied by her husband or a mahram. Identify that this is a condition (shart) for the obligation to perform Hajj, not a pillar.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites multiple hadiths: 'Let no woman perform Hajj except with a mahram' (al-Bazzar) and 'A woman should not travel except with a mahram' (Bukhari and Muslim). Identify the source and type (Sunnah ahad).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form and negation 'la' in the hadith indicate a prohibition, which the Hanafi school interprets as establishing a binding condition. The logical link is that the prohibition implies the absence of the condition renders the act invalid or the obligation lifted.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion: is this condition for the original obligation (wujub) or for performance (ada')? Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir prefers that it is a condition for performance, meaning if a woman lacks a mahram, she is not obligated to perform Hajj at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزوج، أو المحرم (۳) للمرأة
[٣] قوله : والزوج ; عطف على قوله : «أمن الطريق»; أي يشترط أن يكون مع المرأة زوجها أو محرم من محارمها ، وهو من يحرم عليه نكاحها تأييداً ؛ لحديث: «ألا لا يحجن امرأة إلا ومعها محرم»، أخرجه البزار، وفي الصحيحين: «لا تسافر المرأة إلا مع محرم» ، وفي رواية: «إلا ومعها زوجها» (4) ، أو «ذو محرم» (ه)
ويشترط أن يكون كلّ منهما عاقلاً بالغاً غير مجوسي ولا فاسق.
وتجب نفقة محرمها عليها. وهل هذا شرط للوجوب أو وجوب الأداء الذي رجحه في «الفتح» (۳) كون شرط وجوب الأداء عند تحقق الصحة والأمن.
And the husband, or the mahram for the woman. [The commentator] said: His statement 'And the husband' is coordinated with his statement 'safety of the road'; i.e., it is required that the woman be accompanied by her husband or a mahram from her close relatives, who is someone to whom marriage is permanently prohibited. Because of the hadith: 'Let no woman perform Hajj except with a mahram,' narrated by al-Bazzar, and in the Two Sahihs: 'A woman should not travel except with a mahram,' and in another narration: 'except with her husband' or 'with a mahram.' And it is required that each of them be sane, adult, not a Zoroastrian nor a transgressor. And the expenses of her mahram are obligatory upon her. And is this a condition for obligation (wujub) or for performance (ada')? What is preferred in al-Fath is that it is a condition for the obligation of performance when health and safety are realized.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof regarding the condition of a mahram for a woman's obligation to perform Hajj. The text states that a woman must be accompanied by her husband or a mahram (a male relative to whom marriage is permanently forbidden). The commentator explains that this condition is derived from several hadiths, including those in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. The mahram must be sane, adult, and not a Zoroastrian or a transgressor. The woman is responsible for the expenses of her mahram during the journey. There is a discussion among Hanafi scholars whether this condition is for the original obligation (wujub) or for its performance (ada'), with the preferred view in Fath al-Qadir being that it relates to performance when safety and health are present.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): A male relative to whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, fosterage, or marital ties, who accompanies a woman during Hajj.
وجوب (wujub): The original obligation of an act in Islamic law.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act after the condition for its performance is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A woman's obligation to perform Hajj is contingent upon having a husband or mahram accompany her; without one, the obligation is lifted.

Immediate vs Deferred Hajj: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fawr vs tarakhi in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the timing of Hajj and explain the usul principle underlying their disagreement.

Core Idea
The obligation of Hajj is wajib, but whether it must be done immediately hinges on how one interprets the absolute command in usul.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya examines a classic intra-Hanafi debate: does the obligation of Hajj require immediate performance (fawr) or may it be deferred (tarakhi)? The disagreement between the two great disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, is traced back to a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh: the nature of an absolute command (al-amr al-mutlaq). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to see how usul principles generate different fiqh rulings within the same madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State Abu Yusuf's view (fawr: immediate) and Muhammad's view (tarakhi: deferral).
2
Locate the usul basis
Note that later scholars linked this to whether an absolute command implies immediacy or deferral.
This is a key link between usul and fiqh.
3
Work out the practical difference
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: if one delays without excuse, is he sinful according to each view?
Abu Yusuf says sinful; Muhammad says not sinful as long as eventually performed.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Recognize that the Hanafi school prefers fawr (immediate) as the operative opinion for fatwa.
This is the position followed in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فزعم بعض المتأخرين أن هذا الخلاف بينهما مبني على أنَّ الأمر المطلق
ويشترط أن يكون كلّ منهما عاقلاً بالغاً غير مجوسي ولا فاسق.
وتجب نفقة محرمها عليها. وهل هذا شرط للوجوب أو وجوب الأداء الذي رجحه في «الفتح» (۳) كون شرط وجوب الأداء عند تحقق الصحة والأمن.
[1] قوله : مسيرة ; أي مسافة سفر، وهو ثلاثة أيام مع لياليها، وأما ما دون السفر
فيحل لها الخروج من غير زوج ومحرم.
[٢]قوله : على الفور ; بالفتح ; أي بالسرعة ، يعني يجب عليه أن يحج في سنةٍ قدرَ
عليه فيها، ولا يؤخره إلى سنة أخرى.
(۳) قوله : مبني ... الخ ; قد تقرر في كتب الأصول : أنّ الأمر المطلق بشيء أي غير
المقيد بزمان ، هل يقتضي وجوبه على الفور أم على التراخي في العم
So some later scholars claimed that this disagreement between them is based on the fact that the absolute command... And it is required that each of them be sane, adult, not a Zoroastrian nor a transgressor. And the expenses of her mahram are obligatory upon her. And is this a condition for obligation or for performance? What is preferred in al-Fath is that it is a condition for the obligation of performance when health and safety are realized. [1] His statement: 'a distance' i.e., a travel distance, which is three days and their nights. As for less than travel distance, it is permissible for her to go out without a husband or mahram. [2] His statement: 'immediately' (al-fawr) with a fatha; i.e., with haste, meaning he must perform Hajj in the year he is able to, and not delay it to another year. (3) His statement: 'based' etc.; it has been established in books of usul: that the absolute command for something, i.e., not restricted by time, does it require its obligation immediately or with deferral?
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It discusses the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on whether the obligation of Hajj is immediate (fawran) or can be deferred (tarakhi). The text states that some later scholars attribute this difference to a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh: whether an absolute command (al-amr al-mutlaq) that is not restricted by time implies obligation immediately or with deferral. Abu Yusuf holds that Hajj must be performed in the first possible year (fawr), while Muhammad holds that it can be delayed to a later year (tarakhi). The passage also clarifies that the distance for a woman to require a mahram is three days' journey.

Key Terms
فور (fawr): Immediately, without delay. Refers to performing Hajj in the first possible year.
تراخ (tarākhī): Deferral; the view that the obligation can be fulfilled later, not necessarily in the first possible time.
أمر مطلق (amr muṭlaq): An absolute command not restricted by any time condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The interpretation of the absolute command in usul al-fiqh
C) The distance of travel required
D) The financial ability of the pilgrim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that Hajj must be performed immediately (fawr) upon acquiring ability, based on the preferred interpretation that an absolute command implies immediacy.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Immediacy vs. Delay in Hajj Obligation
Explains the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on whether Hajj is obligatory immediately.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the immediacy of Hajj, and identify the practical consequence of each position.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, but does it need to be done immediately or can it be delayed? Two Hanafi giants disagree.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the timing of the Hajj obligation. The source clarifies that the difference is not rooted in a general usul principle, but is an independent issue specific to Hajj. Understanding this dispute helps you appreciate the nuance within the Hanafi school and the practical consequences for a believer's responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the timing of Hajj. Abu Yusuf holds that the obligation is immediate (fawran); Muhammad holds that it is delayed (tarakhi).
Both agree that Hajj is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime.
2
Understand the reasoning
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is caution against losing the opportunity (ihtiraz 'an al-fawt) because Hajj is only possible once a year. Muhammad relies on the principle that an absolute command does not imply immediacy.
The passage notes that this dispute is not based on the usul principle but is a separate issue (mas'alah mubtada'ah).
3
Recognize the independent nature of the issue
The text emphasizes that the disagreement is not a branch of the general rule on 'al-amr al-mutlaq' but is specific to Hajj due to its unique annual occurrence.
This means the ruling cannot be generalized to other obligations.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Abu Yusuf, delaying Hajj without excuse is sinful; according to Muhammad, there is no sin as long as it is performed before death.
In both views, performing Hajj later is considered ada' (performance), not qada'.
5
Note the mufta bihi stance
The text does not definitively settle which view is mufta bihi. Some later scholars chose fawran (e.g., al-Karkhi), others chose tarakhi (e.g., al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Hanifa).
This shows that ikhtilaf within the school is a mercy and both positions have validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن كان بينها وبين مكة مسيرة سفر في العمر مرة على الفور، هذا عند أبي يوسف. وأما عند محمد فعلى التراخي. فزعم بعض المتأخرين أن هذا الخلاف بينهما مبني على أن الأمر المطلق لا يوجب الفور باتفاق بينهما، فمسألة الحج مسألة مبتدأة: فقال أبو يوسف: وجوبه بالفور احتراز عن الفوت، حتى إذا أتى به بعد العام الأول كان أداءً عنده. فمنهم من قال: بالثاني، واختار بعضهم الأول، فالأمر بالحج لما كان وهو يكون للفور عند أبي يوسف له حكم بوجوبه فوراً، وعند محمد له يكون للتراخي، فحكم بوجوبه متراخياً.
If there is a travel distance between her and Mecca, once in a lifetime immediately — this according to Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, it is with delay. So some later scholars claimed that this difference between them is based on the fact that the absolute command does not require immediacy by agreement between them, so the issue of Hajj is an independent issue: Abu Yusuf said its obligation is immediate out of caution against loss, such that if one performs it after the first year it is considered performance according to him. Some said the second (view), and some chose the first. So the command for Hajj, since it is immediate according to Abu Yusuf, he ruled that its obligation is immediate; and according to Muhammad it is for delay, so he ruled that its obligation is delayed.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the obligation of Hajj. The matn states that Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime upon meeting conditions, specifically when there is a travel distance between one's location and Mecca. The commentary then clarifies that the phrase 'on the spot' (على الفور) indicates immediacy according to Abu Yusuf, meaning one must perform Hajj in the first year they are able, and cannot delay to a later year. In contrast, Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that one may delay (على التراخي). The commentator notes that some later jurists mistakenly thought this dispute was based on the general usul principle of whether an absolute command implies immediacy or delay, but he clarifies that this is a separate issue. The reasoning behind Abu Yusuf's view is to prevent the loss of the opportunity, as Hajj only occurs once a year in a specific location. Therefore, if one delays and dies before performing it, they would have sinned. Under Muhammad's view, one is not sinful for delaying as long as they eventually perform it before death. The passage also notes that some later scholars favored the second view (tarakhi), while others favored the first (fawran). This difference does not affect the performance status; in both views, performing Hajj after the first year is considered ada' (performance), not qada' (make-up).

Key Terms
على الفور (‘alā al-fawr): Immediate obligation; must be performed as soon as possible, in the first available opportunity.
على التراخي (‘alā al-tarākhī): Delayed obligation; one may perform it at any time within the lifespan without sinning by delay.
مسألة مبتدأة (mas’alah mubtada’ah): An independent issue not derived from a general usul principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, what is the consequence of delaying Hajj beyond the first year of ability?
A) The Hajj becomes invalid and must be repeated as qada.
B) The person is sinful for delaying, but the Hajj performed later is considered ada (performance).
C) The obligation is lifted entirely.
D) The person must perform Hajj twice to compensate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two valid positions on whether Hajj must be performed immediately or can be delayed, with different consequences for sin.

Hajj: Immediate or Delayed? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Timing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on the timing of Hajj obligation (fawr vs. tarakhi), state the practical consequence (thamara), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The obligation of Hajj is either immediate or delayed; the difference is whether delaying past the first year incurs sin.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether the command for Hajj implies immediacy (fawr) or delay (tarakhi). The issue is not merely theoretical; it determines whether a person who delays Hajj beyond the first year is sinful. The commentary presents both views, their proofs, and the preferred position according to later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf holds that the obligation is immediate (fawr); Muhammad holds that it is on delay (tarakhi) with the condition of not missing.
These are both within the Hanafi school; there are also two narrations from Abu Hanifa himself.
2
Understand the reasoning
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is precaution against missing the once-yearly opportunity. Muhammad's reasoning is that the absolute command does not imply urgency, and the Prophet delayed his own Hajj.
3
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one delays past the first year, Abu Yusuf says he is sinful for the delay; Muhammad says he is not sinful unless death approaches without performing.
Both agree that if one dies without performing, he is sinful by abandoning the obligation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
According to many later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Karkhi, al-Maturidi, and as stated by al-Qari), the immediate view (fawr) is the most correct and relied-upon for fatwa.
This is the operative position in the school, despite the existence of the other view.
5
Apply the distinction to a scenario
Consider a person who becomes obligated in 2025 but performs in 2026. According to the mufta bihi, he is sinful for the delay, but his Hajj is valid as ada', not qada'.
The time for Hajj is the entire life, so performance is always ada' as long as it is done before death.

The book of Hajj. Conditions of Hajj. (1) [It] does not necessitate immediacy by agreement between them. So the issue of Hajj is an independent issue: Abu Yusuf said: Its obligation is immediate, as a precaution against it being missed, such that if he performs it after the first year, it is performance (ada') according to him. Some said the second (view), and some chose the first. So the command for Hajj, since it is absolute, is for immediacy according to Abu Yusuf, so he rules that its obligation is immediate; according to Muhammad it is for delay, so he rules that its obligation is delayed. [Commentary] His statement: 'an independent issue' means it is not built on the disagreement concerning the absolute command. His statement: 'precaution against it being missed' means he only said its obligation is immediate to guard against it being missed; for it only occurs once a year in a specific place, and remaining until that time is a hypothetical matter. His statement: 'such that...' indicates that his intention from its obligation being immediate is not that its time is narrow, so that if he performs it after that year it would be a make-up (qada'), but rather its time is broad and it is the entirety of life, by agreement. Rather, his intention is that if he does not perform it in the first year, he becomes a sinner by delay; according to Muhammad he does not become a sinner, but rather he is at ease in that, but on condition that it is not missed. If he dies before performing it, he sins by abandoning the obligation. (1) The commentator said in al-Tanqih: As for the absolute, it is on delay, because the command came for immediacy and came for delay, so immediacy is not established except by a contextual indication (qarina), and when it is absent, delay is established; not that the command indicates it. (2) It is the saying of Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Abu Hanifa, Malik, and Ahmad. al-Qari transmitted in al-Masalik al-Mutaqassit (p. 27) that it is the correct one, because the time of Hajj is well-known months, so the obligatory thing is Hajj in the months of Hajj absolutely from one's life; so restricting it to immediacy is restricting an absolute, and it is not permissible without evidence. See: al-Bada'i' (2:119) and al-Hajj wa al-‘Umra (pp. 13-14) and others. (3) This is what the texts follow, such as al-Tanwir (2:456) and Bab al-Manasik (p. 4). It is the saying of Abu Yusuf, al-Karkhi, al-Maturidi, and the more sound of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, as stated by Qadi Khan and the author of al-Kafi. al-Qari transmitted in al-Masalik al-Mutaqassit (p. 71) that it is the most correct according to us, and Malik in the mashhur, Ahmad in the azhar, and al-Mazani of the Shafi'is also held it. (4) [Page 548] 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. Then if a boy becomes muhrim and then reaches puberty... According to Muhammad, its obligation is on delay on condition that it is not missed; even if he does not perform in the first year and performs in the second and third, it is performance by agreement. If he does not perform and dies, he is a sinner by agreement. As for Abu Yusuf, it is apparent. As for Muhammad, because it was missed from the first year, and its not being missed in his life is doubtful; so he sins a suspended sin; if he performs after that, the sin lifts according to him; according to Abu Yusuf, the sin for delay does not lift. So the fruit of the dispute is that if he performs after the completion of the first year, he is a sinner for delay according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute analysis. The issue is whether the obligation of Hajj is immediate (fawr) or delayed (tarakhi). The commentator explains that this is an independent issue, not built on the general disagreement about absolute commands. He presents the two positions: Abu Yusuf holds that the obligation is immediate, as a precaution against missing the once-yearly opportunity. Muhammad holds that it is on delay, with a condition that it not be missed. The commentary then clarifies that according to Abu Yusuf, delay beyond the first year is sinful, but the performance is still ada' (timely), not qada'. According to Muhammad, there is no sin for delay until death, but if one dies without performing, both agree on sin. The practical difference (thamara) is sin for delaying past the first year: Abu Yusuf says sinful, Muhammad says not. The commentator also notes that some Hanafi authorities (like al-Karkhi, al-Maturidi) follow Abu Yusuf, while others (like Muhammad, al-Shafi'i) follow the delay view. The passage then transitions to the issue of a minor or slave performing Hajj.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the obligation must be performed as soon as possible without delay.
التراخي (al-tarakhī): Delay; the obligation may be performed later, as long as it is not missed entirely.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarāt al-khilāf): The practical consequence of a legal dispute; here, whether delaying past the first year incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is qada' (make-up) and he is sinful for delay.
B) It is ada' (timely) and he is not sinful.
C) It is ada' but he is sinful for delaying the first year.
D) It is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Hajj is immediate (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school; delaying past the first year incurs sin, but the performance remains valid.

Hajj of a Minor or Slave: Voluntary, Not Obligatory
Ruling with proof: Hajj of minor/slave is tatawwu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a minor or slave's Hajj is valid as tatawwu' and explain the legal reasoning based on the distinction between ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada'.

Core Idea
A minor or slave's Hajj is valid as tatawwu' but never counts as the obligatory Hajj.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a foundational Hanafi rule: those who lack the capacity to be obligated (ahliyyat al-wujub) can still validly perform worship as a voluntary act. Understanding this distinction prevents the common mistake of assuming a child's or slave's Hajj fulfills the Islamic obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the legal question
The passage addresses: Is the Hajj of a minor or slave valid, and does it count as the obligatory Hajj?
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that the Hajj is valid as a voluntary act (tatawwu'), but does not suffice for the obligatory Hajj (fard).
This applies even if the minor later reaches puberty or the slave is freed.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is the distinction between ahliyyat al-wujub (capacity to be obligated) and ahliyyat al-ada' (capacity to perform validly). The minor and slave possess the latter but not the former.
The text states: 'they do not have capacity for obligation, but they have capacity for performance.'
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of ahliyyat al-wujub means no obligation exists. The presence of ahliyyat al-ada' means the act is valid if performed. Therefore, the Hajj is valid but not obligatory.
5
Note the practical consequence
The minor or slave must perform Hajj again after gaining full capacity (bulugh or freedom) to fulfill the obligatory Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[0]- فلو أحرم صبي فبلغ [١]قوله : وجوبه على التراخي ؛ لما ثبت أنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرض عليه الحج في السنة السادسة أو التاسعة من الهجرة ، وأَخَّرَ أداءه إلى السنة العاشرة، ولو كان وجوبُهُ على الفور لما أخره. [٢] قوله : اتفاقاً ؛ لأنه أداه في وقته، وهو زمان حياته. [٣] قوله : يكون آثما اتفاقاً ؛ أما عند أبي يوسف له فلان وجوبه فوري، فيأثم بالتأخير عن العام الأول، فضلاً عما إذا فاته، وأمّا عند محمد له ؛ فلأن وجوبه وإن كان متراخياً لكن يشترط فيه أن لا يفوت، فإذا فاته أثم بتركه فرضاً من الفرائض. (٤) قوله : يأثم بالتأخير؛ أي عن العام الأول، لكن مع ذلك لو حصل منه أداؤه فيما بعده ارتفع عنه الإثم. كذا في «فتح القدير [0]قوله : فلو أحرم ... الخ ؛ تفريع على ما مرَّ من عدم وجوب الحج على غير المكلف، وعلى العبد، وحاصله : أنه إذا أحرم الصبي أو العبد بالحج وأدياه يتأدّى ا منهما تطوّعاً، ولا يجزئهما عن الفرض، فإنّهما وإن لم تكن فيهما أهلية الوجوب، ففيهما أهلية الأداء. (۱) «فتح القدير (٢ : ٤١٣).
[0] So if a boy becomes muhrim and then reaches puberty... [1] His statement: 'Its obligation is on delay'; because it is established that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, Hajj was made obligatory on him in the sixth or ninth year of Hijra, and he delayed performing it until the tenth year. If its obligation were immediate, he would not have delayed it. [2] His statement: 'by agreement'; because he performed it in its time, which is the time of his life. [3] His statement: 'he is a sinner by agreement'; as for Abu Yusuf, because its obligation is immediate, so he sins by delay from the first year, let alone if he missed it. As for Muhammad, because its obligation, though delayed, is conditioned on not being missed, so if he misses it, he sins by abandoning an obligation from among the obligations. (4) His statement: 'he sins by delay'; i.e., from the first year, but even so, if he performs it afterwards, the sin is lifted from him. This is in Fath al-Qadir. [0] His statement: 'So if he becomes muhrim...' is a branch on what passed of the non-obligation of Hajj on the non-mukallaf and the slave. The summary is that if a boy or a slave enters ihram for Hajj and performs it, it is performed by them as a voluntary act, and it does not suffice them for the obligatory (Hajj); for although they do not have capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub), they do have capacity for performance (ahliyyat al-ada').
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the status of Hajj performed by a non-mukallaf (minor) or a slave. The commentator first uses the Prophet's delay of his own Hajj to prove that the obligation is on delay (tarakhi), which is a proof for Muhammad's position. Then he clarifies that when a minor or slave performs Hajj, it counts as a voluntary act (tatawwu'), not as the obligatory Hajj (fard). The reason given is that they lack 'ahliyyat al-wujub' (capacity to be obligated) but possess 'ahliyyat al-ada'' (capacity to perform acts validly). Thus, their Hajj is valid as a supererogatory act, but they must later perform the obligatory Hajj once they become obliged (i.e., after puberty or freedom). The footnote from Fath al-Qadir is cited for the ruling that if an adult delays, the sin for delay is lifted upon performance.

Key Terms
أهلية الوجوب (ahliyyat al-wujūb): Capacity to be obligated to perform an act; a minor and slave lack this for Hajj.
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-adā'): Capacity to perform an act validly; a minor and slave have this for Hajj as a voluntary act.
تطوعاً (tatawwu‘an): Voluntary act; supererogatory worship not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid and suffices for his obligatory Hajj.
B) It is valid as a voluntary act, but he must perform the obligatory Hajj after being freed.
C) It is invalid because a slave cannot perform Hajj.
D) It is valid only if performed with the master's permission.

Key Takeaway
A minor or slave's Hajj is valid as a voluntary act (tatawwu'), not as the obligatory Hajj; they must perform Hajj again after acquiring ahliyyat al-wujub.

Is Hajj Obligatory Immediately or with Latitude? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fawri vs taraakhi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the timing of Hajj obligation and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf: Hajj is fawri (immediate); Muhammad: taraakhi (delayed) – the sin for delay is lifted upon performance only in the latter view.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is the obligation to perform Hajj immediate (fawri) or can it be delayed (taraakhi)? The two great Imams, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on this, each relying on a distinct understanding of the Prophet's own practice. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly advising Muslims on the urgency of Hajj and the consequences of delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The dispute concerns the obligation of Hajj: whether it must be performed as soon as possible (fawri) or may be delayed (taraakhi) as long as it is not completely missed.
Both agree Hajj is wajib once in a lifetime.
2
State each Imam's position
Abu Yusuf holds fawri: delaying without excuse incurs sin, and the sin remains even if later performed. Muhammad holds taraakhi: sin is only incurred if the Hajj is completely missed; sin is lifted upon performance.
The passage presents Muhammad's view first.
3
Analyze the dalil
Muhammad cites the Prophet's delay of his own Hajj from years 6/9 to 10 as evidence that obligation is not immediate. Abu Yusuf's proof is the general principle that an unqualified command implies immediacy.
The passage does not quote Abu Yusuf's dalil explicitly.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If someone delays Hajj beyond the first year and then performs it, Abu Yusuf holds they are still sinful for the delay whereas Muhammad holds the sin is lifted. If they die without performing, both agree they are sinful.
This practical difference affects fatwa and counsel.
5
Note the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities often adopt Abu Yusuf's fawri view as a precaution, but the text in 'Umda al-Ri'aya presents both without tarjih.
The mufta bihi is not settled in this passage.

Source Text

فلو أحرم صبي فبلغوعند محمد له وجوبه على التراخي بشرط أن لا يفوت حتى لو لم يؤد في العام الأول ، وأدى في الثاني والثالث يكون آداء اتفاقا"، ولو لم يؤد، ومـات يكون آثماً اتفاقاً.
أما عند أبي يوسف له فظاهر. وأما عند محمد له ، فلأنه فات عن العام الأول، وعدم فوته في العمر مشكوك ، فيكون آثماً إثماً موقوفاً ، فإن أدى بعد ذلك يرتفعُ الإِثْمُ عنده ، وعند أبي يوسف لا يرتفع الإثمُ للتَّأخير.
فثمرة الخلاف أنه إن أدى بعد تمام العام الأول يأثم بالتأخير عند أبي يوسف الله خلافاً لمحمد
فلو أحرم صبي فبلغ
[١]قوله : وجوبه على التراخي ؛ لما ثبت أنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرض عليه الحج في السنة السادسة أو التاسعة من الهجرة ، وأَخَّرَ أداءه إلى السنة العاشرة، ولو كان وجوبُهُ على الفور لما أخره.
[٢] قوله : اتفاقاً ؛ لأنه أداه في وقته، وهو زمان حياته.
[٣] قوله : يكون آثما اتفاقاً ؛ أما عند أبي يوسف له فلان وجوبه فوري، فيأثم بالتأخير عن العام الأول، فضلاً عما إذا فاته، وأمّا عند محمد له ؛ فلأن وجوبه وإن كان متراخياً لكن يشترط فيه أن لا يفوت، فإذا فاته أثم بتركه فرضاً من الفرائض. (٤) قوله : يأثم بالتأخير؛ أي عن العام الأول، لكن مع ذلك لو حصل منه أداؤه فيما بعده ارتفع عنه الإثم. كذا في «فتح القدير
قوله : فلو أحرم ... الخ ؛ تفريع على ما مرَّ من عدم وجوب الحج على غير المكلف، وعلى العبد، وحاصله : أنه إذا أحرم الصبي أو العبد بالحج وأدياه يتأدّى ا منهما تطوّعاً، ولا يجزئهما عن الفرض، فإنّهما وإن لم تكن فيهما أهلية الوجوب، ففيهما أهلية الأداء.
أو عبد فعتق ، فمضى لم يؤد فرضه، فلو جدد الصبي إحرامه للفرض ثُم وقف جاز عنه بخلاف العبد وفرضُهُ : الإحرام والوقوف بعرفة، وطواف الزيارة. أو عبد فعتق، فمضى لم يؤد فرضه، فلو جدد الصبي إحرامه للفرض ثُمَّ وقف جاز عنه بخلاف العبد) ؛ لأن إحرام الصبي لم يكن لازما ؛ لعدم الأهلية) ، واحرام العبد ،لازم فلا يمكنه الخروج عنه بالشروع في غيرِه.
[1]
(٢)
وفرضه : الإحرام ، والوقوف بعرفة ، وطواف الزيارة (۲٥).
فبعد البلوغ والعتق إن قدرا على الزادِ وغيره وجب عليهما الحج، ولو بلغ الصبي أو عتق العبد بعد أن أحرم في حال صباه ورقيته، فمضى عليه وأتم مناسك حجه لا يكون ذلك فرضاً ؛ لأنّ إحرامه انعقد للتطوع ، فإن نقض الصبي إحرامه بعد البلوغ وجدد إحرامه لحج الفرض جاز عنه بخلاف العبد. [1] قوله : وقف ؛ أشار به إلى أنه لو جَدَّد الإحرام بعد الوقوف بعرفة لا يجزئه ؛ لأن الركن الأعظم للحج وهو الوقوف بعرفة. (۲) قوله : وفرضه ؛ أي المفروض في الحجّ، والمراد به أعم من الركن والشرط. (۳) قوله : الإحرام ؛ هو نيّة الحج بالقلب مع التلبية، وما يقوم مقامها، وهو شرط ابتداء ؛ ولذا جاز تقديمه على أشهر الحج ، وإن كره ، وله حكم الركن انتهاء، حتى لا يجوز لفائت الحج الاستدامة عليه، بل عليه التحلّل بالعمرة، والقضاء في العام القابل، ولو كان شرطاً محضاً لجازت الاستدامة عليه. كذا في «الدر المختار»(۳)، وغيره. [٤]قوله : والوقوف ؛ هذا وما بعده ركنان للحج، والمراد به الوقوف ولو ساعةً من اليوم التاسع من ذي الحجة وليلة العاشر ، وعَرَفة بفتحات، ويقال له : عرفات أيضاً : اسم موضع على اثنا عشر ميلاً من مكة.
[0]قوله : وطواف الزيارة ؛ هو طوافُ البيت يوم النحر أو يومين بعده.
If a boy enters ihram and then reaches puberty... And according to Muhammad, its obligation is delayed (taraakhi) on condition that it not be missed, such that if he did not perform it in the first year, and performed it in the second or third, it is considered performance by agreement. And if he did not perform it and died, he is sinful by agreement. As for Abu Yusuf, it is apparent. As for Muhammad, because he missed it in the first year, and the absence of missing it in his lifetime is doubtful, so he is sinful with suspended sin. If he performs it afterwards, the sin is lifted according to him, but according to Abu Yusuf, the sin for delay is not lifted. So the fruit of the dispute is that if he performs after completion of the first year, he sins for the delay according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. Then if a boy enters ihram and then reaches puberty... He said: its obligation is delayed; because it is established that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made Hajj obligatory in the sixth or ninth year of the Hijra, and he delayed its performance to the tenth year. If its obligation were immediate, he would not have delayed it. He said: by agreement; because he performed it in its time, which is the time of his life. He said: he is sinful by agreement; according to Abu Yusuf, because its obligation is immediate, so he sins for delay from the first year, let alone if he misses it. According to Muhammad, because its obligation is delayed but conditioned on not being missed, so if he misses it, he sins by leaving an obligatory duty. He said: he sins for delay; meaning from the first year, but if he performs it afterwards, the sin is lifted from him. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. He said: then if a boy enters ihram... etc.; This is a branch of the preceding discussion about the non-obligation of Hajj on the non-mukallaf and the slave. The summary: if a boy or slave enters ihram for Hajj and performs it, it is performed as nafl from them, and it does not suffice for the obligatory Hajj, because although they lack eligibility for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub), they possess eligibility for performance (ahliyyat al-ada'). Or a slave is freed, and time passes without him performing his obligatory Hajj. If the boy renews his ihram for the obligatory Hajj then stands at Arafah, it suffices for him, unlike the slave. And the obligations of Hajj are: ihram, standing at Arafah, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Or a slave is freed, and time passes without him performing his obligatory Hajj. If the boy renews his ihram for the obligatory Hajj then stands at Arafah, it suffices for him, unlike the slave; because the boy's ihram was not binding due to lack of capacity, while the slave's ihram is binding, so he cannot exit it by starting another. And its obligation: ihram, standing at Arafah, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Then after puberty and freedom, if they are able to afford provisions and other things, Hajj becomes obligatory on them. If the boy reaches puberty or the slave is freed after having entered ihram during their childhood or slavery, and then they continue and complete their Hajj rituals, that does not count as obligatory Hajj, because their ihram was contracted for nafl. If the boy breaks his ihram after puberty and renews ihram for the obligatory Hajj, it suffices for him, unlike the slave. He said: 'stood'; indicating that if he renews ihram after standing at Arafah, it does not suffice, because the greatest pillar of Hajj is standing at Arafah. He said: 'its obligation'; meaning what is obligatory in Hajj, and it is general including pillar and condition. He said: 'ihram'; it is the intention of Hajj in the heart with talbiyah and what stands in its place. It is a condition at the beginning, thus it is permissible to advance it before the months of Hajj, though disliked. And it has the ruling of a pillar at the end, so that one who misses Hajj may not continue it; rather he must perform tahallul with Umrah and make up in the following year. If it were a pure condition, continuation would be permissible. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others. He said: 'standing'; this and what follows are two pillars of Hajj. It means standing even for a moment on the ninth of Dhul-Hijjah and the night of the tenth. 'Arafah (with fatha) is also called 'Arafat: a place twelve miles from Makkah. He said: 'Tawaf al-Ziyarah'; it is circumambulation of the House on the day of Nahr or the two days after it.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya deals with the rulings concerning a child (sabi) and a slave ('abd) who enter the state of ihram for Hajj before becoming fully obligated (mukallaf). The author first discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding whether the obligation of Hajj is immediate (fawri) or delayed (taraakhi). According to Muhammad, the obligation is delayed on condition that it is not completely missed; if one performs it in subsequent years, it is considered performance by consensus, but if one dies without performing it, he is sinful by consensus. However, the nature of the sin differs: Abu Yusuf holds that sin is for the delay from the first year and is not lifted by later performance, while Muhammad holds that the sin is suspended and lifted upon performance. The practical consequence (thamarat al-khilaf) is that if one performs after the first year, Abu Yusuf considers him sinful for the delay, whereas Muhammad does not.

Then the passage addresses the case of a child entering ihram and then reaching puberty. The author clarifies that the child and slave have ahliyyat al-ada' (capacity for performance) but lack ahliyyat al-wujub (capacity for obligation), so their Hajj is valid as nafl (supererogatory) but does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj. If they later become obligated (by puberty or freedom), they must perform the obligatory Hajj. For the child, if he renews his ihram for the obligatory Hajj after his initial nafl ihram, and then stands at 'Arafah, it suffices ofr his obligatory Hajj, because his initial ihram was not binding (ghayr lazim) due to lack of capacity. In contrast, the slave's ihram is binding (lazim), so he cannot simply exit it and start anew; his performance during slavery counts as nafl, and after freedom he must perform a separate obligatory Hajj.

The passage then defines the obligations (fard) of Hajj as three: ihram, standing at 'Arafah, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. It elaborates that ihram is a condition at the start but has the ruling of a pillar at the end, and standing at 'Arafah is the greatest pillar. Tawaf al-Ziyarah is also a pillar, performed on the day of Nahr or the two days after.

This passage is a typical example of Hanafi fiqh expansion, combining a matn ruling with its proof (dalil from the Prophet's delaying Hajj) and intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
فوري (fawri): Immediate obligation; the duty must be performed as soon as possible without delay.
تراخي (taraakhi): Delayed obligation; the duty can be performed at any time within one's lifespan without immediate sin.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; here, the difference in ruling on sin after performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) of the fawri/tarakhi dispute?
A) Whether Hajj must be performed in Makkah or elsewhere.
B) Whether a person who delays Hajj and then performs it is sinful for the delay.
C) Whether a child's Hajj counts as obligatory.
D) Whether a slave must perform Hajj after freedom.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on fawri vs taraakhi has a real consequence: according to Abu Yusuf, the sin for delay remains even after performance; according to Muhammad, it is lifted.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Hajj of a Child or Slave: Capacity and Ruling after Puberty/Freedom
Ruling on ihram of child/slave and distinction between capacities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada' and apply the ruling that a child or slave's Hajj counts as nafl, not obligatory, and explain the difference in renewing ihram after becoming obligated.

Core Idea
A child or slave has capacity to perform (ahliyyat al-ada') but not to be obligated (ahliyyat al-wujub); their Hajj is nafl, and after puberty/freedom they must perform a separate obligatory Hajj.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a child or a slave enters ihram for Hajj before they are legally obligated. What is the status of that Hajj? Must they repeat it after becoming mukallaf? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the capacity to be obligated (ahliyyat al-wujub) and the capacity to perform valid actions (ahliyyat al-ada'). This distinction is crucial for understanding the rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two capacities
Ahliyyat al-wujub is the capacity to have an obligation imposed; it is lacking in a child and a slave (for Hajj). Ahliyyat al-ada' is the capacity to perform actions validly; a child and slave possess it. Hence their Hajj is valid as nafl.
This is a foundational Hanafi concept.
2
Identify the ruling when child/slave becomes obligated
After puberty (for the child) or freedom (for the slave), Hajj becomes wajib if they have the means. Their previous Hajj during non-obligation does not count as the obligatory Hajj.
They must perform a new Hajj as fard.
3
Distinguish between child and slave regarding renewing ihram
A child can break his nafl ihram after puberty and start a new ihram for the obligatory Hajj; this suffices. A slave cannot; his nafl ihram is binding, so he must complete it and then perform a separate obligatory Hajj later.
The difference is because the child's ihram is not binding (ghayr lazim), while the slave's is binding (lazim).
4
List the three obligations of Hajj
The passage defines the obligations (fard) of Hajj as: ihram, standing at Arafah, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. These are arkan (pillars) or conditions.
Ihram is a condition at start and a pillar at end.
