وإذا لبى ناوياً فقد أحرم، فيتقي الرّفت، والفسوق، والجدال. الرفث : الجماع، أو الكلام الفاحش، أو ذكر الجماع بحضرة النِّساء، فقد رُوِيَ أنّ ابنَ عَبَّاسِ لِما أنشد قوله: ن يَمْشِينَ بِنَا هَمِيْسَا إِنْ يَصْدُقَ الطَّيْرُ نَنِكَ لَمِيسَا قيل له: أترفُتُ وأنت محرم، فقال ابن عباس: إنما الرَّفتُ ما خُوطِبَ به النِّساء. والضمير في هُنَّ يرجع إلى الإبل، والهميس: صوتُ نَعْل أخفافها. [1] قوله: فيتقي؛ شروع فيما يمتنع منه المحرم. [2] قوله: الفسوق؛ بالضمّ مصدر، ويحتمل أن يكون جمع فسق، كعلم وعلوم، كما يشير إليه تفسيرهم بالمعاصي. [3] قوله: الفاحش؛ الذي يكون من دواعي الجماع. [4] قوله: بحضرة؛ بالفتح، أي بمشافهة النساء لا عند غيبوبتهن؛ لأنّ الداعي إلى الجماع هو الأول لا الثاني؛ ولذا لم ير ابن عباس له بشعره المتضمن على ذكر الجماع بأسا. [5] قوله: أنشد؛ إنشاد الشعر قرأته لتغني به، ورفع الصوت. [6] قوله: وهن يمشين... الخ؛ معناه: أنّ الإبل تمشي بنا بالسرعة واليسر، وهذا يؤذن بوصولنا إلى مقصدنا مع الصحة والعافية، فإن صدق هذا الفال نجا مع اللميس، بوصولنا إليها، فالباء في قوله: «بنا» للتعدية، والهميس على وزن كريم: صوت يخرجُ من نعال أقدام الإبل عند وضعها على الأرض ورفعها حالة مشيها المتوسط المعتدل. وقوله: «إن» شرطيّة، وشرطه يصدق بكسر القاف وضم الدال، وفاعل الفعل: «الطير» - وهو بالفتح - الفال وجزاؤه قوله: «ننك»، وهو مضارع بصيغة التكلّم مع الغير، من النيك، يقال: ناك المرأة نيكاً - بالفتح - : فهو نائك؛ أي جامعها وتلذذ بها، فأصله: ننيك على وزن نبيع، حذفت بالياء للجزم. (ورد هذا الأثر في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (3: 310)، واللفظ له، وسنن البيهقي الكبرى» (5: 67): عن أبي العالية عن ابن عباس الله، قال تمثل هذا البيت: وهو محرم، قال: وَهُنَّ يَمْشِينَ بِنَا هَمَيْسَا إِنْ يَصْدُقِ الطَّيْرُ نَنِكَ لَمِيْسا قال: فقيل له: تقول هذا وأنت محرم، فقال: إنما الفحش ما روجع به النساء وهم محرومون.اهـ. واللميس اسم جارية والمعنى نفعلُ بها ما نريدُ إِن يَصْدُقَ الفَأل. والفسوق: هي المعاصي. والجدال: أن يجادل رفيقه، وقيل: مجادلة المشركين في تقديم وقتِ الحج وتأخيره. [11] قوله: جارية؛ أي أمة مملوكة لابن عباس. [2] قوله: هي المعاصي؛ حرمتها وإن كانت في جميع الأحوال، لكنّها في حالِ الإحرام أشد. [3] قوله: أن يجادل؛ أي خصومة مع الرفقاء والخدم والمكارين. [4] قوله: مجادلة المشركين؛ فإنّهم كانوا يُقدِّمون الحج على ذي الحجة ويؤخرونه، وسبب ذلك أنّ الأشهر الأربعة: رجب، وذو القعدة، وذي الحجة، كان القتال فيها محرّماً، وكانوا يعظمونها ويمتنعون عن الغارات والفساد فيها، وكان يشق عليهم في الأشهر المتوالية بسبب طول مدة الامتناع. ومحرم، فكانوا يجعلون سنة المحرم صفر، أو يقولون: جاء صفر في هذه السنة بعد ذي الحجة، وتأخر المحرم، وهذا هو النسيء الذي أبطله الله بقوله: إِنَّمَا النَّي زِيَادَةٌ فِي الكُفْرِ يُضَلُّ بِهِ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يُحِلُّونَهُ عَامًا وَيُحَرِّمُونَهُ عَامًا لِيُوَاطِعُوا عِدَّةَ مَا حَرَّمَ اللهُ فَيُحِلُوا مَا حَرَّمَ اللهُ الآية، وقد كانت الشهور مختطة. بسبب هذا الحساب إلى أن استدار الزمانُ كهيئة عام حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حجة الوداع في السنة العاشرة من الهجرة، وبطل حساب الكفار.
And when he says the talbiyah intending [ihram], he has entered ihram. So he avoids sexual intercourse/obscenity, disobedience, and argumentation. Refath: intercourse, or obscene speech, or mentioning intercourse in the presence of women. It has been narrated that Ibn Abbas, when he recited his verse: 'They walk with us softly... if the bird is true we will have intercourse with Lamisa' it was said to him: 'Do you commit refath while in ihram?' Ibn Abbas said: 'Refath is only what is addressed to women.' The pronoun 'hunna' refers to camels, and 'hamis' is the sound of the hooves of their feet. [1] His saying: 'he avoids' - beginning of what is prohibited for the muhrim. [2] His saying: 'fusuq' - with dammah, a verbal noun, and it may be a plural of fisq, like 'ilm and 'ulum, as their interpretation as sins indicates. [3] His saying: 'fahish' - that which incites to intercourse. [4] His saying: 'bi hadrati' - with fatha, i.e., in the presence of women, not in their absence; because the motivation for intercourse is the former not the latter; hence Ibn Abbas saw no harm in his poetry that mentioned intercourse. [5] His saying: 'anshada' - reciting poetry to sing it and raise the voice. [6] His saying: 'wa hunna yamshina... etc.' - meaning: the camels walk with us quickly and easily, indicating our arrival at our destination with health and well-being. If this good omen is true, we will reach Lamisa. The ba' in 'bina' is transitive. 'Hamis' on the pattern of karim: a sound coming from the soles of camels' feet when placing them on the ground and lifting them in moderate walking. 'In' is conditional, its condition is 'yadq' with kasr of qaf and damm of dal, the subject of the verb is 'al-tayr' - with fatha - the omen, and its answer is 'nanik', which is a future verb in first person plural from 'nayk'. It is said: 'naka al-mar'a naykan' - with fatha - so he is a na'ik, i.e., he had intercourse with her and enjoyed her. Its root is 'nunayk' on the pattern of 'nabi'', the ya' was dropped due to jussive. This narration is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba (3:310) with his wording, and in Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kubra (5:67): from Abu al-Aliya from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, who recited this verse while in ihram. He said: 'Wa hunna yamshina...' and it was said to him: 'You say this while in ihram?' He said: 'Indeed, obscenity is only what is addressed to women while they are deprived.' End. And al-Lamis is the name of a slave girl, and the meaning is we do with her what we want if the omen is true. And fusuq: sins. And jidal: arguing with one's companion, and it is said: arguing with the polytheists about advancing or delaying the time of Hajj. [11] His saying: 'jariya' - i.e., a female slave owned by Ibn Abbas. [2] His saying: 'hiya al-ma'asi' - their prohibition, although it exists in all circumstances, is more severe in the state of ihram. [3] His saying: 'an yujadil' - i.e., arguing with companions, servants, and camel drivers. [4] His saying: 'mujadalat al-mushrikin' - for they used to advance Hajj before Dhu al-Hijjah and delay it. The reason is that the four sacred months: Rajab, Dhu al-Qa'dah, Dhu al-Hijjah, and Muharram, fighting in them was prohibited, and they venerated them and refrained from raids and corruption, and it became difficult for them in consecutive months due to the long period of abstention. So they would make the year of Muharram as Safar, or they would say: Safar came this year after Dhu al-Hijjah, and Muharram is delayed. This is the 'nasi'' which Allah abolished with His saying: 'Indeed, the postponing [of a sacred month] is an increase in disbelief...' (9:37) until the verse. And the months had become mixed up due to this calculation until the time returned as it was in the year of the Prophet's farewell Hajj in the 10th year of hijra, and the calculation of the disbelievers was invalidated.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah, expanding on the three things the muhrim must avoid upon entering ihram: refath, fusuq, and jidal. The author first defines refath as intercourse, obscene speech, or mentioning intercourse in the presence of women. He then narrates an incident of Ibn Abbas to clarify: Ibn Abbas recited a verse containing a reference to intercourse, and when questioned, he explained that refath is only what is addressed directly to women, not general poetry. This shows that the prohibition is context-dependent. The commentary then explains that fusuq means sins in general, and its prohibition is more severe during ihram. Jidal is defined as arguing with companions or, according to another opinion, the polytheists' practice of adjusting the calendar (nasi'). The author details how the polytheists manipulated the sacred months to avoid consecutive prohibitions, which was abolished by the Quranic verse (9:37). The overall ruling is that these three acts are prohibited (haram) for the muhrim, with the understanding that their prohibition is absolute but intensified during ihram.

Key Terms
الرفث (al-rafath): Intercourse, obscene speech, or mentioning intercourse in the presence of women.
الفسوق (al-fusuq): Sins in general, but specifically those that are prohibited at all times, though more severely during ihram.
الجدال (al-jidāl): Argumertation, either with companions or with polytheists during the time of jahiliyyah regarding the timing of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in the passage, what did Ibn Abbas say about his recitation of poetry mentioning intercourse while in ihram?
A) He considered it rafath and repented.
B) He said rafath is only what is addressed directly to women.
C) He forbade all poetry during ihram.
D) He said poetry is always permissible.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid rafath (obscene speech), fusuq (sin), and jidal (argumentation), with rafath specifically being speech directed at women that incites desire.

Prohibition of Killing Land Game During Ihram
Commentary on the prohibition with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing land game while in ihram and identify the Quranic proof and its legal implication.

Core Idea
Killing land game in ihram is haram by direct Quranic command.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key prohibition for the muhrim: killing land game. The ruling is derived from a clear Quranic verse. Understanding this ruling requires knowing what qualifies as 'land game' and the strength of the evidence. This lesson will help you grasp the textual basis and the legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Determine what exactly is prohibited. The text says 'sayd al-barr' – land game. Understand the definition: wild animals normally hunted, excluding domestic animals and sea game.
The distinction between land and sea game is important; sea game is permissible.
2
Locate the proof
The commentator cites Quran 5:95: 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram.' This is the primary evidence.
The verse is directly quoted in the source.
3
Analyse the legal force
The prohibition (nahy) in the verse indicates haram in Hanafi usul, as a definitive text (qati al-thubut) but with zanni al-dalala regarding the scope? Actually, the prohibition is clear, so it is haram.
Hanafi principle: al-nahy yufidu al-tahrim.
4
State the ruling
Conclude that killing land game is haram for the muhrim. This is agreed upon across madhhabs.
The ruling is established and not subject to ikhtilaf in this basic form.
5
Note exclusions
The prohibition applies only to wild land animals that are game. Domestic animals, sea creatures, and harmful animals (e.g., predatory) are exempted by other texts.
The passage does not detail exclusions, but common fiqh knowledge supplements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وقتل صيد البره) [0] قوله : وقتل صيد البرّ - بفتح الباء، وتشديد الراء المهملة -؛ أي الصحراء وغيره، خلاف البحر، والأصل فيه قوله : لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنتُمْ حُرُم . (1) الفأل : بسُكُونِ الهمزة ويجوزُ التَّخْفِيفُ : هُوَ أَنْ تَسْمَعَ كلاماً حَسَنًا فَتَتَيَمَّنَ به ، وإِنْ كَانَ قَبِيحًا فَهُوَ الطَّيَرَةُ، وَجَعَلَ أَبو زَيْدٍ الفالَ فِي سَمَاع الكلامينِ ، وَتَفَاءَلَ بِكَذَا تَفَاؤُلاً. ينظر : «المصباح» ( ص ٤٨٥). (۲) التوبة : من الآية ٣٧. (۳) المائدة : من الآية ٩٥ .
(And killing game of the land). [0] His saying: 'and killing game of the land' - with fatha on the ba' and shadda on the ra' - i.e., the desert and other than it, as opposed to the sea. The basis for it is His saying: 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram.' (1) Al-fa'l: with sukun of the hamza and it is permissible to lighten it: it is hearing good speech and taking it as an omen, and if it is bad, it is tiyara. Abu Zaid made fa'l include hearing both good and bad speech. 'Tafa'ala bi kadha' means taking an omen. See al-Misbah (p. 485). (2) At-Tawbah: from verse 37. (3) Al-Ma'idah: from verse 95.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This section discusses the prohibition of killing land game while in the state of ihram. The author defines 'sayd al-barr' as game from the desert or land, as opposed to sea game. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:95): 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram.' This is a direct command, indicating prohibition. The footnote about fa'l (omen) is likely a remnant from the previous discussion on the Ibn Abbas story, but it is included here editorially. The prohibition is clear: a muhrim may not kill land animals that are considered game. The ruling is haram, and it is based on a definitive text (Quran), which makes it a stronger prohibition.

Key Terms
صيد البر (sayd al-barr): Game found on land, as opposed to sea, including wild animals that are normally hunted.
حرم (hurum): Plural of muhrim, meaning those who have entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
لا تقتلوا (la taqtulu): Do not kill - a prohibition (nahy) in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Fisq and Jidal: Their Meanings and Prohibition in Hajj
Commentary defining fisq and jidal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fisq and jidal as prohibited acts in Hajj and explain why jidal includes disputing about the timing of the sacred months.

Core Idea
Fisq is any sin; jidal is quarrelling with companions or disputing about the pre-Islamic nasi' practice.

In this lesson, we explore two key prohibitions during ihram: fisq (general sins) and jidal (quarrelling). The commentator provides definitions and a historical context for jidal, linking it to the pre-Islamic practice of nasi' (intercalating months). Understanding these terms helps pilgrims avoid acts that diminish the spiritual reward of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term fisq
Locate the definition of fisq in the Arabic text: it is translated as 'sins' (al-ma'asi). Note that the prohibition applies everywhere but is more severe during ihram.
The root verb fasaqa means to deviate from obedience.
2
Identify the term jidal and its two meanings
Find where jidal is defined. The first meaning is quarrelling with one's companion (رفيقه). The second is disputing with polytheists about advancing or delaying the time of Hajj.
Both meanings are considered prohibited during ihram.
3
Understand the historical context of nasi'
Read the explanation about how the polytheists intercalated months to avoid consecutive sacred months, which they found burdensome. This practice is called nasi' and is condemned in the Quran (9:37).
This background clarifies why disputing about timing was a form of jidal.
4
Recognize the ruling and its intensification
Note that the text states 'their prohibition is in all circumstances, but it is more severe during ihram'. Thus fisq and jidal are haram, with heightened prohibition for the muhrim.
The ruling is based on the Arabic phrase 'حرمتها وإن كانت في جميع الأحوال'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفسوق: هي المعاصي. والجدال: أن يجادل رفيقه، وقيل: مجادلة المشركين في تقديم وقتِ الحج وتأخيره. قوله: هي المعاصي؛ حرمتها وإن كانت في جميع الأحوال، لكنّها في حالِ الإحرام أشد. قوله: أن يجادل؛ أي خصومة مع الرفقاء والخدم والمكارين. قوله: مجادلة المشركين؛ فإنّهم كانوا يُقدِّمون الحج على ذي الحجة ويؤخرونه، وسبب ذلك أن الأشهر الأربعة: رجب، وذو القعدة، وذو الحجة، والمحرم، كان القتال فيها محرّماً، وكانوا يعظمونها ويمتنعون عن الغارات والفساد فيها، وكان يشق عليهم في الأشهر المتوالية بسبب طول مدة الامتناع، فكانوا يجعلون سنة المحرم صفر، أو يقولون: جاء صفر في هذه السنة بعد ذي الحجة، وتأخر المحرم، وهذا هو النسيء الذي أبطله الله بقوله: إِنَّمَا النَّسِيءُ زِيَادَةٌ فِي الْكُفْرِ يُضَلُّ بِهِ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يُحِلُّونَهُ عَامًا وَيُحَرِّمُونَهُ عَامًا لِيُوَاطِئُوا عِدَّةَ مَا حَرَّمَ اللهُ فَيُحِلُّوا مَا حَرَّمَ اللهُ الآية، وقد كانت الشهور مختلطة بسبب هذا الحساب إلى أن استدار الزمان كهيئة عام حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حجة الوداع في السنة العاشرة من الهجرة، وبطل حساب الكفار.
And fisq: they are sins. And jidal: to quarrel with one's companion, and it is said: disputing with the polytheists concerning advancing or delaying the time of Hajj. He said: 'they are sins' – their prohibition is in all circumstances, but it is more severe during ihram. He said: 'to quarrel' – i.e., argument with companions, servants, and mule-drivers. He said: 'disputing with the polytheists' – for they used to advance Hajj before Dhu al-Hijjah and delay it, and the reason is that the four sacred months: Rajab, Dhu al-Qa'dah, Dhu al-Hijjah, and Muharram, fighting in them was forbidden, and they venerated them and refrained from raids and corruption during them, and it was hard on them in consecutive months due to the length of abstinence. So they would make the year of Muharram Safar, or say: Safar came this year after Dhu al-Hijjah, and Muharram was delayed. This is the nasi' which Allah abolished with His saying: 'Indeed, the postponing [of sacred months] is an increase in disbelief, by which those who have disbelieved are led astray. They make it lawful one year and unlawful another year to adjust the number of months forbidden by Allah and make lawful what Allah has forbidden' – the verse. And the months had become mixed due to this calculation until the time returned to its state in the year of the Prophet's Hajj, the Farewell Pilgrimage in the tenth year of the Hijrah, and the calculation of the disbelievers was invalidated.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage defines two prohibitions of ihram: fisq (sin) and jidal (quarrelling). The commentator explains that fisq includes all sins, though more severely restricted during ihram. Jidal is explained as two types: quarrelling with companions and the pre-Islamic practice of nasi' (intercalating months) which the Quran condemned. The lengthy note on nasi' shows how the polytheists manipulated the sacred months to avoid consecutive months of peace. The ruling is that fisq and jidal are haram generally but intensified during ihram.

Key Terms
الفسوق (al-fusūq): All acts of disobedience to Allah; sins in general.
الجدال (al-jidāl): Quarrelling or arguing with companions, or disputing with polytheists about the timing of Hajj.
النسيء (al-nasī’): The pre-Islamic practice of intercalating months to adjust the sacred months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fisq (sin) and jidal (quarrelling or disputing about Hajj timing) are forbidden, with heightened prohibition during ihram.

Prohibition of Killing Land Game
Ruling prohibiting the killing of land game for the muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on killing land game for a muhrim and identify the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Killing land game is haram for the muhrim, as explicitly prohibited in the Quran (5:95).

This lesson examines the clear Quranic prohibition against a muhrim killing land game. We will understand the scope of 'land game' as distinct from sea creatures, and see how the Hanafi school derives the ruling directly from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing land game while in ihram. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is Quran 5:95: 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram.'
The verse is directly cited in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative prohibition (lā taqtulū) indicates haram according to Hanafi usul, as the command is in the negative form.
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) indicates that the act is haram.
4
Define the scope
What is meant by 'land game'? It includes all non-domesticated land animals, excluding sea creatures. The commentator specifies that land game includes animals of the desert and other dry land.
The distinction between land and sea is important, as killing sea creatures is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقتل صيد البر. قوله: وقتل صيد البرّ؛ بفتح الباء، وتشديد الراء المهملة؛ أي الصحراء وغيره، خلاف البحر، والأصل فيه قوله تعالى: لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنتُمْ حُرُم.
And killing land game. He said: 'and killing land game' – with a fatha on the ba and a shadda on the ra; i.e., desert and other dry land, as opposed to sea. The basis for it is His saying, exalted: 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram.'
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This is a clear prohibition from the Quran: 'Do not kill game while you are in ihram' (5:95). The commentator specifies that 'land game' includes all animals on dry land, as opposed to sea creatures which are exempted elsewhere. The ruling is that it is haram for the muhrim to kill any land animal that is considered game.

Key Terms
صيد البر (ṣayd al-barr): Game animals found on land (deserts, plains, etc.) as opposed to sea.

Exemption of Sea Game for Muhrim
Ruling exempting sea game from hunting prohibition during ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hunting sea animals while in ihram and identify the Quranic proof for the exemption.

Core Idea
Sea game is halal for the muhrim; the Quran explicitly permits it.

The prohibition of hunting during ihram applies to land animals, but the Quran makes a clear exception for sea creatures. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence from Surah al-Ma'idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is hunting or eating sea animals while in ihram. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah).
This is an exception to the general prohibition of game for a muhrim.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 5:96: 'Lawful to you is the game of the sea...'
The verse explicitly grants permission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لَكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَحْرِ' (lawful to you is the sea game) indicates permissibility. The contrast with 'حُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ' shows that the prohibition of land game does not extend to sea game.
The evidence is clear and unambiguous (qat'i al-dalalah).
4
Note the consensus
All schools of thought agree that sea game is permissible for a muhrim, though some early scholars differentiated between fish and other sea creatures.
The Hanafi position includes all sea animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا البحر. قوله: لا البحر؛ أي لا يحرّم عليه صيد حيوانات البحر؛ لقوله تعالى: لَكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَحْرِ وَطَعَامُهُ مَتَاعًا لَكُمْ وَلِلسَّيَّارَةِ وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا.
Not the sea. He said: 'not the sea' – i.e., the hunting of sea animals is not prohibited for him; because of His saying, exalted: 'Lawful to you is the game of the sea and its food as a provision for you and for travelers, and forbidden to you is the game of the land as long as you are in ihram.'
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
The matn states 'not the sea' meaning the prohibition of game does not apply to sea creatures. The commentator confirms this by quoting the Quranic verse (5:96) which explicitly permits sea game and its food. Thus, muhrim can hunt or eat sea animals without incurring any penalty. This is an exception from the general prohibition.

Key Terms
صيد البحر (ṣayd al-baḥr): All animals that live in the sea, including fish and other marine creatures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Prohibition of Pointing and Showing Game
Ruling prohibiting the muhrim from pointing at or showing game to others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim pointing at or showing game to another, and explain the dalil from the hadith of Abu Qatada.

Core Idea
Pointing at game for another to hunt makes the meat haram for the muhrim — even indirect help invalidates permission.

This passage extends the prohibition of hunting for a muhrim to indirect assistance. The key evidence comes from a hadith where the Prophet asked whether the companions pointed or showed game. Understanding this ruling clarifies how broad the prohibition is and prevents unknowingly violating it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is prohibited for the muhrim? The text specifies two acts: pointing (al-ishārah) to present game and showing (al-dalālah) the location of hidden game. Both are ruled haram.
The act is not limited to verbal instruction; any gesture that assists counts.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Abu Qatada, where the Prophet asked: 'Did you point? Did you show? Did you help?' The companions answered no, so he permitted them to eat the meat. This implies that if they had pointed or shown, the meat would have been unlawful.
This is a sunnah ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's questioning shows that pointing and showing are considered forms of assistance ('awn) in hunting. Since the muhrim may not hunt or assist in hunting, any such participation renders the game meat haram for him.
The hadith connects pointing/showing to helping: 'هل أعنتم؟' (Did you help?).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school takes a strict view that even passive pointing is haram. Some other schools may only prohibit active participation (e.g., physically joining the hunt), but the Hanafi position is that any assistance, even gesture, invalidates the permission.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the stricter position.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is that a muhrim must avoid pointing or showing entirely. If he does any of these, the meat becomes unlawful for him to eat, even if a non-muhrim did the actual hunting.
This is based on the zahir al-riwayah and the clear implication of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإشارة إليه، والدلالة عليه. قوله: والإشارة؛ أي يتجنّب الإشارة إلى الصيد إن كان حاضراً والدلالة عليه إن كان غائباً؛ ليصيده غيره، وذلك لحديث أبي قتادة: إنه صاد حمار وحش، وكان غير محرم وأصحابه محرمون، فقال لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «هل أشرتم؟ هل دللتم؟ هل أعنتم؟» فقالوا: لا، فقال: «إذا فكلوا». أخرج هذه القصة أصحاب الكتب الستة وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة. ودل هذا على أن لحم الصيد حلال للمحرم إذا صاده الحلال؛ أي غير المحرم وأهدى إليه ما لم يشترك في اصطياده بوجه من الوجوه.
And pointing to it, and showing it. He said: 'and pointing' – i.e., he avoids pointing to the game if it is present, and showing it if it is absent, so that another may hunt it. That is due to the hadith of Abu Qatada: He hunted a wild donkey, and he was not in ihram while his companions were in ihram. The Messenger of Allah said to them: 'Did you point? Did you show? Did you help?' They said: No. He said: 'Then eat.' The authors of the six books and others narrated this story with similar wordings. This indicates that the meat of game is halal for the muhrim if a non-muhrim (halal) hunted it and gifted it to him, provided he did not participate in the hunt in any way.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage extends the prohibition to indirect involvement in hunting. The muhrim must not point to game to alert others, nor show its location. The hadith of Abu Qatada is the key evidence: when the Prophet asked the muhrim companions if they pointed, showed, or helped, and they answered no, he permitted them to eat the meat. This proves that if a muhrim does any of these actions, the meat becomes haram for him. Conversely, if a non-muhrim hunts alone and gifts the meat, the muhrim may eat it.

Key Terms
الإشارة (al-ishārah): Pointing to game that is visible to direct others' attention to it.
الدلالة (al-dalālah): Showing the location of game that is hidden or not immediately visible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Did you hunt?
B) Did you point, show, or help?
C) Did you eat the meat?
D) Did you see the game?

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid any action, even pointing, that assists in hunting; otherwise the game meat becomes unlawful.

Prohibition of Perfume During Ihram
Ruling prohibiting the use of perfume during ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on applying perfume during ihram and explain the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Using perfume on body or clothes is haram for the muhrim; the pilgrim must be disheveled and unkempt.

The pilgrim in ihram is commanded to set aside worldly adornment as a symbol of humility before Allah. The act of perfuming—applying any scented substance—directly contradicts this state. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage prohibits 'al-taṭayyub' (perfuming). Determine the hukm level: is it haram, makruh, or something else?
The Hanafi school considers it haram, as derived from the hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'The pilgrim is disheveled and unkempt.' Find its source and transmission level.
Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah; it is ahad hadith, so thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith prohibits perfume. The description implies absence of perfume, so using it contradicts the recommended state.
The phrase 'al-sha'ith al-tafil' means unkempt and without scent. Applying perfume negates this.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds this prohibition as haram, and it is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتطيب. قوله: والتطيب؛ أي استعمالُ الطيب في بدنِهِ ولباسه؛ لحديث: «الحاج الشعث التفل» أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة.
And perfuming. He said: 'and perfuming' – i.e., the use of perfume on his body and his garment; due to the hadith: 'The pilgrim is disheveled and unkempt' narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
The matn prohibits 'perfuming' (al-tayyib) during ihram. The commentator explains this includes applying any scented substance to the body or clothing. The proof is the hadith describing the ideal pilgrim as 'al-sha'ith al-tafil' (disheveled and unkempt), implying absence of perfume. Therefore, using perfume is a prohibited act (haram) for the muhrim. The hadith emphasizes the state of humility and avoidance of worldly adornment.

Key Terms
التطيب (al-taṭayyub): The act of applying perfume (tib) to the body or clothing.
الشعث التفل (al-sha'ith al-tafil): Describing the pilgrim as having disheveled hair and being unkempt, without perfume or grooming.

Permissibility of Sea Hunting in Ihram
Clarifies the permissibility of sea hunting in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sea hunting for the muhrim and identify the Quranic proof that establishes its permissibility.

Core Idea
Sea hunting is explicitly permitted for the muhrim by the Quran; land game is prohibited.

The first ruling discussed in this passage clarifies that the prohibition of hunting in ihram applies only to land game. Sea creatures are excluded by clear Quranic text. The commentary emphasizes that the muhrim may hunt or eat from the sea without restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hunting sea animals (sayd al-bahr). The ruling is mubah (permissible) for the muhrim, explicitly stated as 'لا يحرّم عليه' (it is not prohibited).
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The proof is Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96: 'Lawful to you is game from the sea and its food as provision for you and for travelers, but prohibited to you is game from the land as long as you are in ihram.'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'أُحِلَّ' (it is made lawful) indicates clear permissibility. The contrast with 'وَحُرِّمَ' (prohibited) for land game confirms that sea game is excluded from the general prohibition.
The prohibition of land game is specific to ihram, but sea game is explicitly made lawful.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds this as settled (zahir al-riwayah) based on the qat'i dalil. No ikhtilaf is reported regarding this permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام لا البحر، والإشارة إليه ، والدلالة عليه ، والتطيب لا البحر ، والإشارة إليه ، والدلالة عليه ، والتطيب بضمتين إلى محرمون. قوله : لا البحر ؛ أي لا يحرّم عليه صيد حيوانات البحر ؛ لقوله تعالى : {أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَحْرِ وَطَعَامُهُ مَتَاعًا لَكُمْ وَلِلسَّيَّارَةِ ۖ وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا} . قوله : والإشارة ؛ أي يتجنّب الإشارة إلى الصيد إن كان حاضراً والدلالة عليه إن كان غائباً ؛ ليصيده غيره، وذلك لحديث أبي قتادة رضي الله عنه : إنه صاد حمار وحش، وكان غير محرم وأصحابه محرمون ، فقال لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «هل أشرتم؟ هل دللتم؟ هل أعنتم ؟ فقالوا : لا ، فقال : إذا فكلوا» ، أخرج هذه القصة أصحاب الكتب الستة وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة. ودل هذا على أن لحم الصيد حلال للمحرم إذا صاده الحلال ؛ أي غير المحرم وأهدى إليه ما لم يشترك في اصطياده بوجه من الوجوه. قوله : والتطيب ؛ أي استعمالُ الطيب في بدنِهِ ولباسه ؛ لحديث: «الحاج الشعث التفل» ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة ، والشَّعِث: بفتح الأول وكسر الثاني
The book of Hajj, chapter of Ihram: Not the sea, and signaling to it, and directing to it, and perfuming. [Repetition with pronunciation note: 'with two dhammas to 'muhrimun''. He said: 'Not the sea' means he is not prohibited from hunting sea animals; due to His saying: 'Lawful to you is game from the sea and its food as provision for you and for travelers, but prohibited to you is game from the land as long as you are in ihram.' He said: 'And signaling' means he should avoid signaling to game if it is present and directing to it if it is absent, so that another may hunt it; due to the hadith of Abu Qatada: He hunted a wild donkey while he was not in ihram and his companions were in ihram, and the Messenger of Allah said to them: 'Did you signal? Did you direct? Did you assist?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat.' This was transmitted by the authors of the six books and others with similar wording. This indicates that the meat of game is lawful for the muhrim if a non-muhrim (halal) hunted it and gifted it to him, as long as he did not participate in its hunting in any way. He said: 'And perfuming' means using perfume on his body or clothing; due to the hadith: 'The pilgrim is disheveled and dusty.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah. 'Ash'ath': with fath of the first and kasr of the second.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding three prohibitions (and one permission) in ihram. First, it clarifies that hunting sea animals is not prohibited for the muhrim; the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:96) explicitly permits it. Second, it prohibits signaling or directing another person to game, drawing from the incident of Abu Qatada where the Prophet allowed eating the game only because no signaling or assistance occurred. Third, it prohibits applying perfume, based on the hadith describing the pilgrim as 'ash'ath tafil' (unkempt and unscented). The commentary emphasizes that these actions are forbidden for the one in ihram, and that the permissibility of eating game hunted by a non-muhrim hinges on the muhrim's non-participation in the hunt.

Key Terms
صيد البحر (sayd al-bahr): Hunting or catching sea creatures, permissible for the muhrim.
أُحِلَّ (uhilla): It is made lawful, an imperative indicating permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which verse permits sea hunting for the muhrim?
A) Surah al-Baqarah 2:173
B) Surah al-Ma'idah 5:96
C) Surah al-An'am 6:121
D) Surah al-Nahl 16:115

Key Takeaway
Sea hunting is permissible for the muhrim based on explicit Quranic text.

Prohibition of Signaling and Perfume in Ihram
Explains the prohibition of signaling/directing and perfuming in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim signaling to game or applying perfume and identify the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A muhrim may not signal or direct others to game, nor apply perfume; these actions violate the state of ihram.

The commentary continues with two more prohibitions: signaling/directing to game and using perfume. Both are derived from hadith: the story of Abu Qatada establishes that signaling invalidates the permission to eat gifted game, and the hadith 'ash'ath tafil' describes the desired state of a pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibitions
The first is الإشارة (signaling) to visible game and الدلالة (directing) to hidden game, so another may hunt it. The second is التطيب (perfuming) on body or clothes.
2
Locate the hadith proofs
For signaling: hadith of Abu Qatada where the Prophet questioned if they had signaled, directed, or assisted, and allowed eating only when they said no. For perfume: hadith 'الحاج الشعث التفل' (the pilgrim is disheveled and dusty).
3
Analyze the implication of the hadith
The Abu Qatada hadith indicates that if a muhrim participates in the hunt by signaling, the meat becomes prohibited for him. The perfume hadith shows that refraining from perfume is a requirement of ihram.
4
Summarize the Hanafi position
Both actions are haram (prohibited) for the muhrim, based on these hadith. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text

كتاب الحج باب الإحرام لا البحر، والإشارة إليه ، والدلالة عليه ، والتطيب لا البحر ، والإشارة إليه ، والدلالة عليه ، والتطيب بضمتين إلى محرمون. قوله : لا البحر ؛ أي لا يحرّم عليه صيد حيوانات البحر ؛ لقوله تعالى : {أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَحْرِ وَطَعَامُهُ مَتَاعًا لَكُمْ وَلِلسَّيَّارَةِ ۖ وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا} . قوله : والإشارة ؛ أي يتجنّب الإشارة إلى الصيد إن كان حاضراً والدلالة عليه إن كان غائباً ؛ ليصيده غيره، وذلك لحديث أبي قتادة رضي الله عنه : إنه صاد حمار وحش، وكان غير محرم وأصحابه محرمون ، فقال لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «هل أشرتم؟ هل دللتم؟ هل أعنتم ؟ فقالوا : لا ، فقال : إذا فكلوا» ، أخرج هذه القصة أصحاب الكتب الستة وغيرهم بألفاظ متقاربة. ودل هذا على أن لحم الصيد حلال للمحرم إذا صاده الحلال ؛ أي غير المحرم وأهدى إليه ما لم يشترك في اصطياده بوجه من الوجوه. قوله : والتطيب ؛ أي استعمالُ الطيب في بدنِهِ ولباسه ؛ لحديث: «الحاج الشعث التفل» ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة ، والشَّعِث: بفتح الأول وكسر الثاني

Prohibitions for the Muhrim: Nail Cutting and Covering Face/Head
Commentary on nail cutting and face/head covering prohibitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nail cutting and covering face/head in ihram, explain the general principle, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Any act of adornment is prohibited for the muhrim; nail cutting and covering face/head are haram.

In this lesson, we examine two specific prohibitions for the muhrim (one in ihram): cutting the nails and covering the face and head for men, and for women, covering the head but not the face with a cloth. These are based on the general principle that acts of beautification are forbidden, and specific hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The commentator states that all acts of adornment and refinement are prevented from the muhrim. This is the overarching rule that governs the specific prohibitions.
2
Analyze the ruling on nail cutting
Cutting nails is an act of adornment, so it is prohibited (haram) for the muhrim. This is derived by analogy from the general principle.
The text mentions 'qalam al-azfar' as included.
3
Examine the hadith for covering face/head
The hadith: 'Do not cover his face nor his head...' is cited. In Hanafi usul, the imperative negative (لا تخمروا) indicates prohibition (tahrim).
This hadith is specific to men.
4
Distinguish the ruling for women
Women cover their heads but must not wear a niqab or gloves, as per another hadith. They are permitted to cover the head but not the face with a cloth thrown over.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario (e.g., a muhrim man covering his face), the student should state it is haram and cite the hadith.
Practice this in the tasks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية وقَلْمَ الإظفار وستر الوجه والرأس، وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخِطْمِي، وقصها مغبر الرأس والتَّقِل : على وزن الشعث تارك الطيب وغيره، من التفل وهو الريح الكريهة. قوله : وقلم الأظفار ; بالفتح جمع ظفر ، بالضم بالفارسية: ناخن، والقلم ; بالفتح : القطع، والأصل في هذا أنّ كلَّ ما هو من أفعال الزينة والتعيش يمنعُ عنه المحرم، للحديث المذكور، فيدخلُ فيه قص الظفر، وحلق شعر الرأس واللحية وتقصيره، وشعر غيرهما من الأعضاء، وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي ; بالكسر أي ما مزج به وبغيره، واستعمال الدهن ولبس ثوب مطيب ومصبوغ بصبغ فيه طيب ونحو ذلك. قوله : وستر الوجه والرأس؛ لحديث: لا تخمروا وجهه ولا رأسه، فإنّه يبعث ملبياً يوم القيامة قاله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في محرم توفي بعرفات سنة حجة الوداع ، أخرجه مسلم وغيره، وهذا للرجل. وأما المرأة فتستر الرأس، لكن لا تلقي الثوب على الوجه واليدين، قال رسول الله : «لا تتنقب المرأة ولا تلبس القفازين» ، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره. قوله : بالخطمي ونحوه ؛ مما يغسل به الشعر ويزال به الوسخ ، وأما نفس غسله بدون ذلك فلا بأس به، فإنّه لا يزيده إلا شعثاً، ثبت ذلك عن عمر وعن أبي أيوب ، ورفع ذلك إلى النبي ، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ»، وغيره. قوله : وقصها ؛ أي قطع اللحية كلاً أو بعضاً، وإن كان قطع ما زاد على القبضة جائزاً في غير الإحرام، ثبت ذلك عن ابن عمر برواية مالك، بل عن عمر
The mainstay of attention on the explanation of al-Wiqayah: And cutting the nails, and covering the face and head, and washing his head and beard with khitmi, and trimming it — dusty head and unkempt: on the weight of 'ash'ath, leaving perfume and other things, from 'tafil' which is foul smell. He said: 'And cutting the nails' — with fath (fatha) plural of 'zufur' (nail), with damm: 'nakhun' in Persian; 'qalam' with fath: cutting. The principle in this is that everything that is an act of adornment and refinement is prevented from the muhrim, due to the aforementioned hadith. So it includes cutting the nail, shaving the hair of the head and beard and shortening it, and hair of other limbs, and washing his head and beard with khitmi — with kasr (kasra) i.e. what is mixed with it and other things, and using oil, and wearing a perfumed garment or one dyed with a dye containing perfume, and the like. He said: 'And covering the face and head' due to the hadith: 'Do not cover his face nor his head, for he will be raised on the Day of Resurrection saying labbayk' — said by the Messenger of Allah concerning a muhrim who died at Arafat during the Farewell Hajj, narrated by Muslim and others. This is for the man. As for the woman, she covers her head, but she does not throw the cloth over her face and hands; the Messenger of Allah said: 'The woman should not wear a niqab nor wear gloves,' narrated by Abu Dawud and others. He said: 'With khitmi and the like' i.e. what is used to wash the hair and remove dirt. As for washing it without that, there is no harm in it, for it only increases disheveledness. This is established from Umar and Abu Ayyub, and it is elevated to the Prophet, narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta and others. He said: 'And trimming it' i.e. cutting the beard entirely or partially, although cutting what exceeds the grip is permissible outside ihram, established from Ibn Umar in the narration of Malik, rather from Umar.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on prohibitions for the muhrim. It covers four actions: (1) Cutting nails — prohibited as part of adornment. (2) Covering the face and head for men — prohibited based on the hadith about the muhrim who died; for women, covering the head is required but covering the face with a cloth (niqab) and wearing gloves are prohibited. (3) Washing the head and beard with khitmi (a cleansing agent) — prohibited because it removes dirt contrary to the ideal of being 'sha'ith'; however, washing without such agents is permissible as it only increases disheveledness. (4) Trimming the beard — prohibited, though cutting beyond a fistful is allowed outside ihram. The overarching principle is that any act of beautification or refinement is forbidden for the muhrim.

Key Terms
قلم الأظفار (qalam al-azfar): Cutting the nails; an act of adornment prohibited for the muhrim.
ستر الوجه والرأس (satr al-wajh wa al-ra's): Covering the face and head; prohibited for men, but women cover the head but not the face with a cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a man in ihram covering his head with a cloth?
A) Permissible if needed
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Nail cutting and face/head covering for men are haram in ihram, while women must cover the head but cannot wear niqab or gloves.

Prohibitions for the Muhrim: Washing with Khitmi and Beard Trimming
Commentary on washing with khitmi and beard trimming prohibitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing the head and beard with khitmi and trimming the beard in ihram, and distinguish between washing with and without cleansing agents.

Core Idea
Washing with a cleansing agent (khitmi) is haram; washing without it is permissible. Beard trimming is haram; cutting beyond a fistful outside ihram is allowed.

This lesson continues the examination of prohibitions for the muhrim, focusing on washing the head and beard with a cleansing agent like khitmi, and trimming the beard. The commentator distinguishes between washing with such agents—which removes dirt and is thus prohibited—and washing without them, which is permissible as it increases disheveledness (sha'ath). The beard trimming is prohibited completely in ihram, though outside ihram cutting beyond a fistful is allowed based on companion practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on washing with khitmi
Washing the head and beard with khitmi (a plant-based soap) is prohibited because it cleanses and refines, contrary to the state of the muhrim who should appear disheveled.
2
Note the exception: washing without khitmi
Washing with plain water without any cleansing agent is permissible, as it only increases disheveledness. This is established from the actions of Umar and Abu Ayyub, and even attributed to the Prophet.
This is a key nuance.
3
Examine the ruling on beard trimming
Trimming the beard, whether partially or fully, is prohibited for the muhrim. This falls under the general prohibition of removing hair.
4
Distinguish between ihram and non-ihram
Outside ihram, cutting the beard beyond a fistful is permissible, as reported from Ibn Umar. But in ihram, even partial trimming is haram.
The fistful rule is a sunnah for beard length outside ihram.
5
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Given scenarios, the student should decide whether an act is permissible or prohibited and cite the relevant proof.

Source Text

قصها (qassaha): Trimming or cutting the beard; prohibited in ihram even partially.

Prohibition of Grooming Acts in Ihram
Commentary on prohibitions of grooming acts for the muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which grooming acts are prohibited for a muhrim and explain the underlying principle and its proof.

Core Idea
All acts of adornment and cleanliness are prohibited for the muhrim, as they contradict the state of ihram.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the prohibition of nail cutting, hair removal, and perfumed washing for a person in ihram. The commentator derives the ruling from the principle that any act of adornment or cleanliness is forbidden, based on a hadith. He also highlights an exception: washing with plain water is allowed, as it increases dishevelment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Acts
List the specific acts mentioned in the passage: cutting nails, shaving or cutting hair (head, beard, other limbs), washing with khitmi (perfumed plant), and trimming the beard.
Also includes covering the face/head and using oil or perfumed garments.
2
Understand the General Principle
The commentator states that 'everything that is from acts of adornment and cleanliness is prohibited for the muhrim.' Grasp this principle: the state of ihram requires leaving worldly beautification.
This principle is the basis for the prohibition of all listed acts.
3
Locate the Dalil
The passage references 'the aforementioned hadith' as proof. Although not quoted, this hadith (recorded by Malik) establishes the prohibition. Recognize that the ruling is grounded in a textual proof.
The hadith is likely: 'The muhrim should not cut his nails, shave his hair, etc.'
4
Note the Exception
The commentator specifies that washing the head without any perfumed substance (just water) is permissible and even encouraged to increase dishevelment (sha'ath).
Dishevelment is a desired quality in ihram.

وقَلْمَ الإظفار وستر الوجه والرأس، وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخِطْمِي، وقصها) مغبر الرأس والتَّقِل : على وزن الشعث تارك الطيب وغيره، من التفل وهو الريح الكريهة.
[١]قوله : وقلم الأظفار ؛ - بالفتح جمع ظفر ، بالضم بالفارسية: ناخن، والقلم - بالفتح : القطع ، والأصل في هذا أنّ كلَّ ما هو من أفعال الزينة والتعيش يمنعُ عنه المحرم، للحديث المذكور، فيدخلُ فيه قص الظفر، وحلق شعر الرأس واللحية وتقصيره، وشعر غيرهما من الأعضاء، وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي - بالكسر أي ما مزج به وبغيره، واستعمال الدهن ولبس ثوب مطيب ومصبوغ بصبغ فيه طيب ونحو ذلك.
(٣) قوله : بالخطمي ونحوه ؛ مما يغسل به الشعر ويزال به الوسخ ، وأما نفس غسله بدون ذلك فلا بأس به، فإنّه لا يزيده إلا شعثاً، ثبت ذلك عن عمر وعن أبي أيوب ، ورفع ذلك إلى النبي ، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ»، وغيره.
[٤] قوله : وقصها ؛ أي قطع اللحية كلاً أو بعضاً، وإن كان قطع ما زاد على القبضة جائزاً في غير الإحرام، ثبت ذلك عن ابن عمر برواية مالك، بل عن عمر
And cutting the nails, covering the face and head, and washing his head and beard with khitmi, and trimming it (the beard). Dusty head and unkempt: on the weight of 'sha'ath' (disheveled), one who leaves perfume and other things, from 'tafal' which is foul smell. [1] His saying: 'And cutting the nails' - with fatha, plural of 'zufr' with damma, in Persian 'nakhun', and 'qalam' with fatha means cutting. The basis of this is that everything that is from acts of adornment and cleanliness is prohibited for the muhrim, due to the aforementioned hadith. So it includes cutting the nails, shaving the hair of the head and beard and shortening it, and hair of other limbs, and washing his head and beard with khitmi - with kasra, meaning anything mixed with it or with other things, and using oil, and wearing a perfumed garment or one dyed with a dye that has perfume, and similar things. [3] His saying: 'with khitmi and the like' - those things used to wash hair and remove dirt. As for washing without that, it is fine, because it only increases dishevelment. This is established from Umar and Abu Ayyub, and it is attributed to the Prophet, recorded by Malik in al-Muwatta and others. [4] His saying: 'and trimming it' - i.e., cutting the beard entirely or partially, although cutting what exceeds the fistful is permissible outside of ihram; this is established from Ibn Umar according to Malik's narration, rather from Umar.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the prohibitions for a muhrim. The original matn lists prohibited acts: cutting nails, covering face/head, washing with khitmi, trimming beard. The commentator explains 'qalam' (cutting) and states the principle: all acts of adornment/cleanliness are prohibited, based on a hadith. This includes cutting nails, shaving hair from any body part, using perfumed substances like khitmi, using oil, and wearing perfumed/dyed clothes. He clarifies that washing without perfumed substances is allowed, as it increases dishevelment (sha'ath), which is desirable in ihram. This is supported by Umar and Abu Ayyub. Finally, trimming the beard is prohibited during ihram, even though trimming beyond a fistful is permissible outside ihram.

Key Terms
قلم الأظفار (qalam al-azfar): Cutting the nails; prohibited for muhrim.
خطمي (khitmi): A plant used to wash hair, considered perfumed; prohibited for muhrim.
قص اللحية (qass al-lihyah): Trimming the beard; prohibited for muhrim even partially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Washing head with water only
C) Using perfumed oil on hair
D) Trimming the beard

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must avoid all acts of adornment and cleanliness, including nail cutting, hair removal, and using perfumed substances; plain washing is allowed.

Prohibition of Covering Face and Head in Ihram: Rulings for Men and Women
Commentary on the prohibition of covering face and head for muhrim men, and rules for women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for men and women in ihram regarding covering the face, head, and hands, and cite the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A man in ihram must not cover his head or face; a woman covers her head but must not wear a niqab or gloves.

The state of ihram imposes specific dress restrictions to maintain the spirit of humility and equality. For men, covering the head or face nullifies this state; for women, the rules are nuanced: they must cover their heads but avoid face veils and gloves. This lesson unpacks the hadith evidence and the Hanafi position on these prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being prohibited: covering the face and head for men, and wearing niqab and gloves for women. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
Note the gender distinction: the prohibition for men is absolute; for women it is partial (they cover the head but not the face/hands).
2
Locate the dalil for men
The hadith of the muhrim who died at Arafat: the Prophet said, 'Do not cover his face nor his head.' This is recorded by Muslim. The imperative 'لا تخمروا' indicates prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (single narrator), giving zanni thubut, but it is accepted as authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the ruling to women
Women must cover their heads (like in salah) but are prohibited from wearing a niqab (face veil) or gloves. The evidence is the hadith in Abu Dawud: 'The woman should not wear a niqab nor gloves.'
This means a woman's face and hands (except the palms up to wrists) remain uncovered during ihram.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school holds that wearing a niqab or gloves is haram for women. Some Shafi'i scholars allow covering the face if the cloth does not touch the skin, but the Hanafi view is the mufta bihi.
The practical difference: a Hanafi woman must ensure her face is completely uncovered, while a Shafi'i woman might cover it loosely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وستر الوجه والرأس؛ لحديث: لا تخمروا وجهه ولا رأسه، فإنّه يبعث ملبياً يوم القيامة» قاله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في محرم توفي بعرفات سنة حجة الوداع ، أخرجه مسلم وغيره، وهذا للرجل. وأما المرأة فتستر الرأس، لكن لا تلقي الثوب على الوجه واليدين، قال رسول الله : «لا تتنقب المرأة ولا تلبس القفازين»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره.
And covering the face and head: due to the hadith: 'Do not cover his face nor his head, for he will be raised on the Day of Judgment in the state of talbiyah.' The Messenger of Allah said this concerning a muhrim who died at Arafat during the Farewell Pilgrimage. Recorded by Muslim and others. This is for men. As for the woman, she covers her head, but she does not throw cloth over her face and hands. The Messenger of Allah said: 'The woman should not wear a niqab nor gloves.' Recorded by Abu Dawud and others.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage explains the prohibition of covering the face and head for a muhrim. The commentator cites the hadith of the man who died at Arafat in ihram; the Prophet instructed not to cover his head or face. This applies to men. For women, the rule differs: she must cover her head (as in salah), but she should not cover her face (niqab) nor wear gloves. The hadith for women prohibits niqab and gloves. Thus, a woman's face and hands remain uncovered during ihram.

Key Terms
تخمروا (tukhamiru): to cover (from khamr meaning covering); used in hadith for covering head/face.
نقاب (niqab): face veil covering nose and mouth; prohibited for woman in ihram.
قفازان (qafazayn): gloves (dual); prohibited for women in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) She must uncover it
C) She may choose to cover or uncover
D) She must cover it with a cloth that does not touch her face

Key Takeaway
A man in ihram must not cover his head or face; a woman covers her head but must not wear a niqab or gloves, as established by explicit hadith proofs.

Prohibition of Sewn Garments and Perfumed Dyes in Ihram
Ruling with proof: prohibition of sewn garments and perfumed-dyed cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing sewn garments and dyed cloth in ihram, and apply the exception for non-perfumed dyes and faded perfume.

Core Idea
Sewn garments and cloth dyed with perfume are haram in ihram; only unsewn and non-perfumed cloth are allowed.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi position on what a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) may wear. The source passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya lists specific prohibited items and provides the Prophetic evidence, along with a critical distinction: cloth dyed with perfumed substances is prohibited until the perfume fades, but non-perfumed dyes are permissible. The rule applies to all sewn garments by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited items
From the matn, list the garments explicitly mentioned: shirt, trousers, closed cloak, turban, skullcap, leather socks. Understand that the commentator extends this to 'all sewn garments' (kull makhit).
These are garments that are tailored to the body; unsewn cloth like izaar and rida are not prohibited.
2
Understand the evidence
The prohibition is based on the Prophet's prohibition of these items for the muhrim, recorded by the Sunni imams. This ahad hadith provides the proof.
3
Distinguish perfumed vs non-perfumed dyes
The text specifies that cloth dyed with a perfumed substance (like saffron or 'usfur) is prohibited, but cloth dyed with a non-perfumed dye is allowed. The exception 'except after the removal of its perfume' means that if the perfume has faded, the cloth becomes permissible.
This shows the ruling is based on the presence of perfume, not the color itself.
4
Apply the analogy to all perfumed cloth
The commentator explains that the hadith prohibition of cloth touched by saffron or 'usfur applies to any cloth with perfume. The 'illa (effective cause) is the perfume, so any perfumed cloth is included.
5
Recognize the scope of 'makhit'
The phrase 'yaltahiq biha kull makhit' (every sewn garment attaches to this ruling) means the prohibition is general for all sewn garments, not just the listed ones. This is a qiyas-based extension.
The Hanafi school is strict on this: any garment sewn to fit the body is prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبس قميص وسراويل، وقباء وعمامة ، وقلنسوة، وخُفِّين) ، وثوباً صُبغ بما له طيب إلا بعد زوال طيبه
[١] قوله : ولبس قميص ... الخ ؛ لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى المحرم عن لبس هذه الأشياء، أخرجه الأئمة السنّة، ويلتحق بها كل مخيط.
[٢) قوله : صبغ بما له طيب ؛ بالكسر : أي الثوب المصبوغ بصبغ ذي طيب، ولذا «نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عــن ثـوب مسه زعفران أو عصفر، كما أخرجه الطحاوي وغيره، ولا يمنع ثوب مصبوغ بصبغ ليس كذلك ، ثبت ذلك . عن طلحة بن عبيد الله الله في «الموطأ»، وغيره.
And wearing a shirt, trousers, a closed cloak, a turban, a skullcap, two leather socks, and a cloth dyed with something that has perfume, except after the removal of its perfume.
[1] His saying: 'and wearing a shirt...' etc.: because it is narrated that the Prophet prohibited the muhrim from wearing these things, recorded by the Sunni imams, and every sewn garment is attached to this ruling.
[2] His saying: 'dyed with something that has perfume' - i.e., the cloth dyed with a dye that has perfume. Therefore, the Messenger of Allah prohibited cloth that has been touched by saffron or 'usfur, as recorded by al-Tahawi and others. He does not prevent a cloth dyed with a dye that is not like that; this is established from Talha ibn Ubaydullah in al-Muwatta and others.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage explains the prohibition of wearing sewn garments and perfumed-dyed cloth. The matn lists specific items: shirt, trousers, closed cloak, turban, skullcap, leather socks, and cloth dyed with a perfumed substance. The commentator states the basis is the Prophetic prohibition, and all sewn garments fall under this rule (yaltahiq biha kull makhit). For dyed cloth, the prohibition is specifically for cloth dyed with perfumed substances like saffron (za'faran) and 'usfur. However, cloth dyed with non-perfumed substances is allowed, as reported from Talha ibn Ubaydullah. The exception 'except after the removal of its perfume' means if the perfume has faded, wearing such cloth is permissible.

Key Terms
مخيط (makhit): sewn garment; anything sewn to fit the body.
زعفران (za'faran): saffron, a perfume; used to dye cloth; prohibited for muhrim.
عصفر ('usfur): a plant used for yellow dye; also perfumed; prohibited for muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sewn garments are absolutely prohibited for the muhrim, and cloth dyed with perfume is prohibited until the perfume fades; non-perfumed dye is allowed.

Permissibility of Bathing for a Muhrim
Clarification that bathing is not prohibited for the muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bathing for a muhrim and identify the evidence from the Prophet and his companions.

Core Idea
A muhrim may bathe freely; it is not prohibited.

You might have heard that a person in ihram cannot bathe, thinking it might break the state or involve perfuming. This lesson clarifies the correct Hanafi position: bathing is permissible, as established by the Prophet's practice. Let's examine the textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states 'la al-istihmam' – at first glance this seems to prohibit bathing. But the commentator immediately clarifies it means it is not prohibited. So the act is istihmam (bathing) and the hukm is mubah (permissible).
2
Locate the evidence
The commentator cites 'lithubut dhalik 'an Rasul Allah wa ashabih' – this is established from the Prophet and his companions. This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) from practice.
The text does not specify a particular hadith; it relies on established practice.
3
Understand the scope of permissibility
The commentator specifies that istihmam means ightisal (washing) whether in a bathhouse (hammam) or elsewhere. So any form of washing is allowed.
This includes washing with water only; using scented soap would be an issue, but that is not covered here.
4
Check for exceptions
The ruling is general – no exceptions are mentioned. However, note that bathing that involves harming or removing hair intentionally might be subject to other rules (e.g., fidyah). But the simple act of washing is mubah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا الاستحمام [٤] قوله : لا الاستحمام ؛ أي لا يمنعُ للمحرم الدخول في الحمام، والمراد به الاغتسال كان في الحمام أو في غيره ؛ لثبوتِ ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه
No bathing. [4] His saying: 'No bathing' - i.e., it is not prohibited for the muhrim to enter the bathhouse; what is meant is washing, whether in the bathhouse or elsewhere, because this is established from the Messenger of Allah and his companions.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage clarifies that bathing is not prohibited for the muhrim. The matn states 'la al-istihmam' meaning it is not prohibited. The commentator explains that entering a bathhouse (hammam) is allowed, and istihmam refers to washing (ightisal) anywhere. This is supported by the practice of the Prophet and his companions. Thus, a muhrim may bathe freely, as it does not conflict with the state of ihram.

Key Terms
استحمام (istihmam): bathing; entering a bathhouse; washing the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Prohibited Garments and Permissible Bathing for the Muhrim
Prohibition of wearing sewn garments and dyed clothes in Ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific garments prohibited for the Muhrim and explain why bathing is not included.

Core Idea
The Muhrim must not wear tailored garments or perfumed cloth, but may bathe freely.

In this passage, the author lists the specific clothing items forbidden during Ihram and extends the ruling to all sewn garments. He also clarifies that cloth dyed with perfume is prohibited until the scent fades, while bathing remains permissible. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the key distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited garments
List the six items explicitly mentioned: shirt, trousers, cloak, turban, cap, and khuffs. Note that these are all tailored (makhit).
The list is illustrative; any garment sewn to fit the body is included by analogy.
2
Understand the dalil
The prohibition is based on a prophetic hadith (recorded by the imams of Sunnah) that forbids the Muhrim from wearing these items. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition from the Prophet (saw) obligates haram.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut but qati dalala in this context.
3
Extend to all makhit
The commentator states 'and every sewn garment is annexed to them.' This means any garment cut and sewn to the body shape is prohibited by analogy (qiyas).
Accessories like belts or money belts that are not body-conforming are not included—the text explicitly permits tying a money belt.
4
Differentiate perfumed vs non-perfumed dye
Cloth dyed with a perfume (like saffron or safflower) is prohibited until the scent fades. Non-perfumed dye is allowed, as reported from Talhah.
The prohibition here is on the scent, not the cloth itself. Once the scent is gone, the cloth is permissible.
5
Note the permissibility of bathing
The text explicitly states 'la al-istihmam'—bathing is not prohibited. This applies whether in a bathhouse or elsewhere, based on the practice of the Prophet and Companions.
Seeking shade and tying a money belt are also explicitly permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام ولبس قميص وسراويل، وقباء وعمامة، وقلنسوة، وخُفَّين، وثوباً صبغ بما له طيب إلا بعد زوال طيبه لا الاستحمام [1] قوله: ولبس قميص... الخ؛ لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى المحرم عن لبس هذه الأشياء، أخرجه الأئمة السنة، ويلتحق بها كل مخيط. [2] قوله: صبغ بما له طيب؛ بالكسر: أي الثوب المصبوغ بصبغ ذي طيب، ولذا نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ثوب مسه زعفران أو عصفر، كما أخرجه الطحاوي وغيره، ولا يمنع ثوب مصبوغ بصبغ ليس كذلك، ثبت ذلك عن طلحة بن عبيد الله في الموطأ وغيره. [3] قوله: لا؛ أي لا يبقى الاستحمام وما بعده مما عطف عليه، وهو الاستظلال وشد هميان منصوب، أو لا يكره الاستحمام... الخ، وحينئذ كله مرفوع. [4] قوله: لا الاستحمام؛ أي لا يمنع للمحرم الدخول في الحمام، والمراد به الاغتسال كان في الحمام أو في غيره؛ لثبوت ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه.
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: And wearing a shirt, trousers, a cloak, a turban, a cap, khuffs, and a cloth dyed with perfume except after its scent disappears does not prevent bathing. [1] His statement: 'And wearing a shirt... etc.' because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the Muhrim from wearing these things, recorded by the imams of the Sunnah, and every sewn garment is annexed to them. [2] His statement: 'dyed with perfume' (with kasra): meaning the cloth dyed with a dye that has perfume, therefore the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade a cloth touched by saffron or safflower, as recorded by al-Tahawi and others, and a cloth dyed with a dye that is not so is not prevented; that is established from Talhah ibn Ubaydullah in al-Muwatta and elsewhere. [3] His statement: 'does not' meaning that what follows is not prevented, namely bathing and what is conjoined to it, which is seeking shade and tying a money belt (mansub), or bathing is not disliked... etc. [4] His statement: 'does not prevent bathing' meaning that the Muhrim is not prevented from entering the bathhouse, and what is meant is washing, whether in the bathhouse or elsewhere, due to its being established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his Companions.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the prohibitions of Ihram regarding clothing. The matn first lists specific garments the Muhrim must not wear: shirt (qamis), trousers (sarawil), cloak (qaba'), turban (imamah), cap (qalansuwah), and khuffs (leather socks). The commentator notes that these are individually forbidden based on the prophetic prohibition narrated from Ibn Umar and others, and that any tailor-made garment (makhit) that conforms to the body is included by analogy. Then the text adds that a cloth dyed with a perfume such as saffron or safflower is also prohibited until the scent fades, citing the hadith forbidding cloth touched by these substances. However, cloth dyed with non-perfumed dye is permitted, as reported from Talhah. The final clause 'la al-istihmam' clarifies that bathing is not prohibited for the Muhrim, whether in a bathhouse or elsewhere, proven by the practice of the Prophet and his Companions. The commentator explains that the word 'la' negates the prohibition for what follows, namely bathing, seeking shade, and tying a money belt, all of which are permissible. Thus the passage establishes the limits of clothing prohibitions in Ihram while explicitly allowing bathing.

Key Terms
مخيط (makhīṭ): Any garment sewn to fit the body (tailored), including shirts, trousers, etc. that are prohibited for the Muhrim.
طيب (ṭīb): Perfume or fragrant substance used in dying cloth; such cloth is prohibited until the scent fades.

Key Takeaway

Permissible Acts in Ihram: Shade and Money Belt
Ruling with proof for permissibility of shade and belt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking shade and tying a money belt in Ihram and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
A Muhrim may seek shade under any cover and tie a money belt – necessity overrides the sewn garment prohibition.

In this lesson, we examine two actions often questioned by pilgrims: entering shade and using a sewn money belt. Many assume these violate the Ihram restrictions, but Hanafi fiqh permits them based on the practice of the Companions and the principle of necessity. Understanding these rulings helps pilgrims fulfil their rituals without unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their rulings
The passage states that seeking shade (istizlal) under a house or camel litter is permissible, and tying a money belt (himyan) around the waist is also permitted. Both are mubah (permissible) for the Muhrim.
The ruling is explicit, not speculative.
2
Examine the proof for shade
The commentator cites the practice of Caliph Uthman ibn Affan, who had a tent pitched for him during his own Ihram. This is recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah. In Hanafi usul, the act of a Companion is a proof (hujjah) when not contradicted.
This shows shade is allowed even for the head, as long as nothing touches the head directly.
3
Examine the proof for the money belt
The permission for the money belt comes from a group of Companions and Successors. It is allowed due to necessity (darurah)—the pilgrim needs to carry money securely. The belt is sewn, but necessity makes it permissible.
Compare: other sewn garments are prohibited, but necessity changes the ruling.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab dimension
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'is) may forbid intentionally shading the head or wearing sewn items even if needed. The Hanafi position prioritizes ease and necessity, based on the broader objectives of the Law.
The practical consequence: a Hanafi pilgrim can use an umbrella or tent, while a Shafi'i may not.

Source Text

والاستظلال ببيت ومحمل وشد هميان في وسطه وأكثر التلبية متى صلى أو علا شرفاً أو هبط وادياً أو لقي ركباناً أو أسحر [1] قوله: والاستظلال؛ أي الدخول في ظل سقف البيت أو جداره أو الهودج أو الفسطاط أو نحو ذلك، فقد كان لعثمان فسطاط يضرب له في إحرامه، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة. [2] قوله: وشد هميان؛ هو بكسر الهاء وسكون الميم: شيء يشبه تكه السراويل، يشد على الوسط، وتوضع فيه الدراهم، وقد ثبتت الرخصة فيه عن جمع من الصحابة والتابعين للضرورة، وقد بسطنا الكلام في هذا المقام في التعليق الممجد. [3] قوله: وأكثر؛ ماض من الإكثار؛ أي لبى خلف كل صلاة، وعند الصعود على شرف – وهو بفتحتين - موضع عال، وعند الهبوط؛ أي النزول في الوادي؛ أي المكان المنخفض عند ملاقاة الركبان بالضم؛ أي الراكبين المسافرين، وعند دخول وقت السحر.
And seeking shade with a house and a camel litter, and tying a money belt around his waist, and frequently reciting the talbiyah whenever he prays, or ascends a high place, or descends a valley, or meets riders, or at dawn. [1] His statement: 'and seeking shade' means entering under the shade of a roof of a house or its wall, or a howdah, or a tent, or the like. Uthman had a tent pitched for him during his Ihram, recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah. [2] His statement: 'and tying a money belt' (himyan) is with kasr of the ha and sukun of the mim: something like the waistband of trousers, tied around the waist, in which dirhams are placed. Permission for it has been established from a group of Companions and Successors due to necessity, and we have expanded the discussion on this point in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad. [3] His statement: 'and frequently' is past tense from ikthar (to do much); meaning he recited the talbiyah after every prayer, and when ascending a high place (sharaf, with two fatha, meaning a high location), and when descending (hobūt) into a valley (low place), and when meeting riders (rukbān, with dammah, meaning traveling riders), and at the time of dawn (sahar).
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage presents a set of permissible and recommended actions for the person in Ihram. The matn states that seeking shade under a house or a camel litter (mahmil) is allowed, despite the general prohibition of covering the head. The commentator explains that 'seeking shade' (istizlal) includes entering the shade of a roof, wall, howdah, or tent (fustat). He supports this by citing the practice of Caliph Uthman, who had a tent pitched during his own Ihram, as recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah. Next, the text permits tying a money belt (himyan) around the waist, even though it is a sewn item. The commentator describes it as a belt like a trouser string, used to carry coins, and notes that it is allowed due to necessity (darurah), with evidence from many Companions and Successors. Finally, the passage highly recommends (istihbab) increasing the talbiyah (the proclamation 'Labbayk...') at specific occasions: after each obligatory prayer, when ascending a high place (sharaf), when descending into a valley (wadi), when meeting fellow travelers (rukban), and at dawn (sahar). The commentator clarifies each term and the proper times for this sunnah act. Thus, the Muhrim may use shade and belts for practical needs, and should maximize the talbiyah at these virtuous moments.

Key Terms
استظلال (istiẓlāl): To seek shade, i.e., to enter under a roof, tent, or other covering to avoid sun, permissible for Muhrim despite head covering prohibition.
همیان (himyān): A money belt or girdle tied around the waist, often sewn, but permitted for the Muhrim due to necessity.

Recommended Times for Talbiyah in Ihram
Recommendation to frequently recite talbiyah at specific times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five recommended occasions for reciting the talbiyah and explain why each is significant.

Core Idea
Frequent talbiyah after prayers, on heights, in valleys, meeting riders, and at dawn is a confirmed sunnah.

Talbiyah is the hallmark of Ihram, and the Prophet ﷺ encouraged its repetition. This lesson details the specific moments when a Muhrim should increase the recitation, as derived from the practice of the Companions. Knowing these occasions helps the pilgrim maximize the spiritual rewards and follow the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling for talbiyah
Talbiyah is a sunnah (recommended) act for the Muhrim. The passage specifically recommends increasing it (ikthar) at certain moments.
It is not obligatory (wajib) but highly desirable.
2
List the five occasions
The text mentions: 1) after every obligatory prayer (when the prayer is finished), 2) when ascending a high place (sharaf), 3) when descending into a valley (wadi), 4) when meeting riders (rukban), and 5) at dawn (sahar).
Each occasion marks a change in situation or time.
3
Understand the rationale
These are moments of transition and heightened consciousness. Each encourages remembrance of Allah and affirmation of the pilgrimage intent.
The talbiyah proclaims one's response to Allah's call.
4
Apply in practice
A pilgrim today can recite talbiyah after each fard prayer, when climbing the hills in Mina or Arafat, when descending into the valley of Muzdalifah, when meeting other pilgrims on the road, and at the time of sehri (pre-dawn).
There is no harm in reciting at other times, but these are emphasized.
